Sports News

Revision of Jiangsu Province Secondary School Physical Education Implementation Outline (1) – Announced by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education for the 25th Year 84

The revised Jiangsu Province Secondary School Physical Education Implementation Outline for the 25th year has been submitted by the Jiangsu Department of Education to the Ministry of Education for approval and record. The original text is as follows:

General Principles (1) All public and private secondary schools in this province must, from this year onwards, implement strict physical education training for all students in the school in accordance with the provisions of this outline. (2) The implementation of physical education training in each school should take the following items as the ultimate goal, and simultaneously or in stages use practical methods to achieve real results: 1. Enable each student's physique to develop fully; 2. Enable each student's spirit to be lively and resolute; 3. Enable each student's physical ability to be sufficient to cope with all environments; 4. Enable each student's behavior to naturally conform to group discipline; 5. Enable each student's life to have vigorous vitality. (3) From this year onwards, each school should use the power of the school's physical education administrative organization to establish a plan and practically promote physical education training for all students in the school. (4) From this year onwards, each school should continue to prepare a physical education budget, reduce unnecessary waste, and increase necessary construction. (5) From this year onwards, each school should formulate a concrete plan to expand physical education building facilities, implement it in stages, in order to meet the needs of the implementation of this outline. (6) From this year onwards, each school should, in accordance with the Ministry's promulgated physical education mileage standards for secondary schools and the provisions of this outline, formulate detailed plans for all physical education activities such as physical education courses, morning exercises, extracurricular sports, and intra-school sports competitions, and earnestly promote them. (7) From this year onwards, each school should, in accordance with the provisions of this outline, implement strict assessment of students' physical education training achievements; those who fail shall not be promoted or graduate. (8) From this year onwards, each school should earnestly conduct student physical examinations, at least once per semester, as a basis for implementing physical education training. (9) The promotion of this outline shall be the joint responsibility of the principals, directors of teaching affairs, directors of student affairs, directors of general affairs, directors of junior high school, teachers in charge of each grade, physical education teachers, boy scout instructors, military instructors, and school doctors of each school. All faculty and staff members of the school have the obligation to assist. (10) The achievements of the promotion of this outline will be assessed by provincial and county school inspectors and special personnel at any time as a basis for rewards and punishments.

Administration (1) Each school should organize a physical education committee to preside over the school's physical education administration. (2) The physical education committee shall be composed of the principal, the director of teaching affairs, the director of student affairs, the director of general affairs, the director of junior high school, physical education teachers, boy scout instructors, military instructors, school doctors, and enthusiastic faculty and staff members. The principal shall appoint one physical education teacher as a standing committee member, who shall meet at least twice each semester. Its functions and powers are as follows: 1. At the beginning of the academic year, determine the physical education plan for the year; 2. Prepare and review the expenditure plan and expenditure status of physical education funds; 3. Plan the expansion or renovation of sports venues and equipment; 4. Review and approve various measures for the management of physical education activities throughout the school; 5. Seek progress in school hygiene and improvement of student life; 6. Other matters related to the improvement of physical education throughout the school. (4) The standing committee member of the physical education committee, under the order of the principal and the entrustment of the physical education committee, shall plan and implement the school's physical education affairs in accordance with the provisions of this outline, and compile the implementation situation into a work report on a regular basis and submit it to each physical education committee meeting for review. (5) For schools that have organized a physical education committee, there is no need to establish a physical education subject meeting; the matters that should be carried out shall be carried out by the physical education committee on its behalf. (6) Each school should lead all students in the school to organize various sports groups so as to achieve the effect of popularization and development. (7) The sports groups organized by the students of each school should be officially registered with the education committee. Regardless of any activities, they should be subject to the control and guidance of the physical education committee. The registration and management methods shall be formulated by each school itself.

Funding (1) Each school shall compile a separate expenditure plan and expenditure status of the physical education fees paid by students, the physical education funds in the school budget, and other funds belonging to physical education by the physical education committee, and submit them to the principal separately at the beginning and end of the academic year. (2) Each school's physical education funds should be used exclusively for the needs of physical education consumption and equipment, and shall not be misappropriated at will. (3) The distribution standard of each school's physical education funds is as follows: 1. Physical education consumption expenses, such as the purchase of sports equipment, the repair of equipment, etc., shall not be more than 50% of the total; 2. Physical education business expenses, such as the school sports meet and external competitions, etc., shall not be more than 20% of the total; 3. Physical education equipment expenses, such as the construction of sports venues, the purchase of fixed equipment, etc., shall not be less than 30% of the total.

Equipment (1) Each school should follow the minimum standards for physical education equipment in each school promulgated by the department, prepare a phased expansion plan, together with the funding budget, and submit them separately for approval. (2) Each school should make full use of the open space on campus to arrange the physical education environment, so as to arouse students' interest and achieve results invisibly. (3) Each school should try to make use of the natural environment outside the nearby school for the school's physical education training. (4) The sports venues and equipment of each school should be opened to the public for amateur sports as much as possible within the scope of possibility, but detailed management measures should be formulated. (5) Each school should have considerable indoor sports equipment so that students can have an appropriate amount of activities during rainy and snowy periods.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Formulates Competition Instructions for the Municipal Games, with 1303 Athletes from 139 Schools Participating, and the Guarantee Deposits of Each School Should Be Paid as Soon as Possible in Exchange for the Issuance of Number Cloths 85

The 4th Municipal Games of this city, sponsored by the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, will be held at the Municipal Central District Stadium starting on the 22nd of this month. In addition, the guarantee deposits that each school should pay must be paid as soon as possible. In the future, the number cloths will be issued based on the receipt of the guarantee deposit. The competition instructions of the conference have been formulated, and are recorded as follows:

Participation Statistics A total of 122 men and 2 women in the open group, 46 male students from 6 universities and 10 female students from 2 universities in the university group, 37 male students from 2 physical education colleges and 6 female students from 2 physical education colleges in the physical education school group, 23 male students from 1 physical education teacher school and 30 female students from 2 physical education teacher schools, 328 male students from 39 high schools and 112 female students from 17 high schools, 288 male students from 44 junior high schools and 197 female students from 24 junior high schools, 90 men and 12 women in the national arts group, totaling 139 schools and 1303 athletes.

Competition Instructions (1) When athletes participating in track and field and national arts competitions register, each athlete must pay a guarantee deposit of 20 cents in national currency. After the meeting, the number cloth will be returned at the Municipal Stadium, the office of this association. If the number cloth is lost, or the athlete registers but does not show up, or shows up but does not participate in the competition, or violates the rules and is disqualified, the deposit will not be returned. (2) All athletes must place the two number cloths issued to them (the same as specified on the order form), one on the chest and one on the back, otherwise they will not be allowed to participate in the competition. (3) Athletes must report to the roll call station on time to register and participate in the competition, otherwise they will be deemed to have forfeited the right to compete. (4) Athletes who have already forfeited the right to compete shall not rejoin the competition. (5) Athletes found to be in violation of the rules of this association on the field will be immediately disqualified from the competition. (6) In which group each athlete competes in the previous event, the athlete shall not move up or down any group in the next event. If any such situation is found, all the points earned will be cancelled. (7) Athletes who intentionally push, bump, or run diagonally, and hinder the progress of others during the competition, will be disqualified regardless of whether it occurs in the preliminary round, semi-final, or final. (8) Athletes shall not use equipment or other strong stimulants during the competition to enhance their actions and seek victory. (9) There must be at least six athletes in the final. If it is not possible in fact, this is not an exception. (10) At least two places will be taken in each group in the preliminary round and semi-final. (11) Coaches, staff, and personnel who do not participate in sports competitions from each school are not allowed to enter the competition venue and must visit in the stands. (12) If there are too many participants in each sports event and it cannot be completed in one competition, a preliminary round and semi-final should be held before the final. (13) Athletes who have already forfeited the right to compete shall not rejoin the competition. (14) The clothing of athletes in the open group shall be made by the individual, and the clothing of athletes in the school group shall be made by the school. It must be neat and clean. (15) The order of each contestant in each competition shall be drawn by the conference host. (16) Athletes in each field event should try to jump and throw in accordance with the order arranged by the conference. (17) Athletes in field events who are also participating in track events may, with the permission of the field event referee, be allowed to try to jump and throw out of order. (18) If the results of each field event are similar, the similar athletes will compete one more time, trying to jump or throw, raising or lowering, until a winner is determined. (19) The starting position or the running line of track athletes shall be determined by drawing lots by the allocation section. (20) If an athlete has any protests, etc., they shall submit a written protest and pay a guarantee deposit of 5 yuan to the adjudication committee for adjudication within one hour of the occurrence. If the adjudication committee deems that the aforementioned protest is without sufficient reason, the guarantee deposit paid may be confiscated. (21) The protest letter of the open group shall be signed and sealed by the athlete himself, and a guarantor from the sports community of this city shall be found. The protest letter of the school group shall be signed and sealed by the physical education teacher and the responsible personnel in the administration of the athlete's school. (22) After the protest letter has been decided by the adjudication committee, there shall be no further protests.

Zhejiang Department of Education Randomly Tests Secondary School Students' Academic Performance, This Semester Will Be Implemented by Appointing School Inspectors to Preside 92

The Zhejiang Department of Education has already started the 25th academic year, and specially revised the old rules for randomly testing the graduation performance of secondary school students in accordance with the actual situation, and appointed school inspectors to preside over the tests, and will go to various secondary schools to hold them. In addition, the Department ordered all public and private secondary schools and county and city governments to comply with the regulations, which will be implemented immediately. The regulations are recorded as follows:

Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education Revised Regulations for Randomly Testing Secondary School Students' Academic Performance, Article 1, These regulations are formulated for randomly checking the usual academic performance of secondary school students in this province. Article 2, The random testing of secondary school students shall be presided over by the director of the Department, who shall appoint the Department's school inspectors to go to various secondary schools. Article 3, The subjects of the random test shall be limited to (1) the subjects with the most failing grades in the school's semester, and (2) the subjects that have not been tested. Article 4, The test questions for each subject shall be prepared or selected temporarily by the presiding school inspector. Article 5, When the school inspector arrives at the specified grade and class of each secondary school for random testing, the class may be ordered to suspend classes temporarily to wait for the test. After the test, classes shall resume as usual. Article 6, The principal and the director of teaching affairs may enter the examination room to assist the school inspector during the test. Test papers may be borrowed from the school's temporary test papers. Article 7, During the test, students taking the test shall only be allowed to bring necessary stationery. Other books and notes shall not be allowed. Article 8, During the test, students taking the test shall listen to the instructions of the school inspector and shall strictly abide by the examination room rules. Article 9, The test papers shall be sealed and sent to the Department by the school inspector, and shall be handled by the personnel designated by the director of the Department. Article 10, These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Dr. Xue Guangqian on Italy's Renaissance and China (II) 100

In summary, the key lies first in:

Sound Economic Institutions

The Italian nation, through government-appointed personnel, has organized twenty-two industrial cooperation bureaus, bringing together consumers, sellers, and producers to work together to achieve balanced industrial and economic development. In addition, there are nine major trade associations for agriculture, industry, commerce, banking, insurance, and the free professions. Labor and management are organized separately to adjust their respective interests, striving for the overall improvement of the national economy. Because of this strict organization and these institutions, the government commands the whole nation as if it were a single person, directing it as easily as moving an arm. Its youth training is grounded in reality and pragmatism, offering much that is worthy of emulation. When the Italo-Ethiopian War was launched, the world assumed that the climate in East Africa was too hot and that marching there would be difficult. Little did they know that Mussolini had been training young people for fourteen years, having them train shirtless in the scorching sun at noon every day without interruption. Thus, they had become a formidable army capable of withstanding heat. Therefore, since the beginning of the war, although the army was far from home and faced economic hardship, it remained unwavering and ultimately achieved the final result. Although its aggressive militarism is difficult to sympathize with, the principles of national revival and construction are universally applicable throughout history. Today, China has suffered to the extreme, surviving nine deaths to reach one life. Success depends on self-reliance. The path to self-reliance begins with cultivating two types of strength:

Spiritual and Material

Modern warfare is not just a war of military force, but also a war of manpower, financial resources, material resources, and time. Therefore, how to tighten belts and save on food and clothing to cultivate more material strength for the country is the responsibility of every individual today. Given China's current poverty and the urgency of critical construction, everyone must not only be honest and serve the public, but must also take a step further by being economical and making one dollar do the work of two, and one minute do the work of two. Only then can we turn around the nation's destiny and have hope for the future. In terms of spiritual strength, we must cultivate a force that supports the leader until death, so that all national talent and wisdom can be concentrated under a single leader, sharing a common goal, taking the same steps, and uniting sincerely to fight together. We must recognize that Italy's ability to stand tall and dominate today is due to the success of Mussolini's iron-fisted politics. But Mussolini's ability to act decisively and do as he pleased was due to the countless "Mussolinis" throughout the country who supported him and sincerely defended him, enabling him to hold the reins and use them freely. We must realize that the vastness of our country's territory is like the whole of Europe. In the past, Napoleon, despite his great talent, failed to unify the European continent despite several expeditions. Our unified country is not comparable to the fragmented countries of Europe. However, given the low level of national education, the underdeveloped transportation, and the different lifestyles between the north and south, achieving unity is not easy. Today, with the pacification of Guangdong and Guangxi, and the unity of the whole country, it can be inferred that Generalissimo Chiang's talent surpasses even Napoleon's. Therefore, today, we should believe in doctrines and support the leader in spirit, and tighten belts and be economical in material terms. This is the only way to save ourselves from danger and achieve self-reliance in the future. Belief in doctrines and support for the leader should not be empty talk, but should start with oneself, set an example, and extend it to others. Tightening belts and being economical should not focus on theory, but should start immediately, put into practice, and be implemented earnestly. If everyone can be genuine and not pretentious, tell the truth, do real things, and match words with deeds, then the revival of China may be within reach. (End)

Yarn and Cotton Prices Reach New Heights; Cotton Yarn Reaches 218 Yuan This Month; Short Covering Becomes More Urgent and Market Prices Soar 104

The yarn market was weak in the morning but rose sharply in the afternoon, and the trend remains tense. The shortage of yarn and the nervousness of short sellers caused buyers to swarm in as soon as the market tightened. The market price quickly jumped. It was reported in the afternoon that there were over 2,700 bales of 20-count Samsung yarn in the warehouse. This cotton yarn was said to be unwanted, but because the current stock has been exhausted, the Tianjin gang came to search for it and bought 500 bales, causing the selling price to rise by two yuan. As a result, the market was shaken and prices soared. The October price has reached a high of 218 yuan.

Prices Rise Two to Three Yuan Each Month

In the morning, the spot yarn market opened with long positions showing strong interest in near-term contracts, rising by four to seven jiao. Far-term contracts showed mixed gains and losses, fluctuating up and down by two to three jiao. After the second session, it was reported that yarn sales had decreased, and customer activity was lighter, causing market sentiment to weaken. However, due to the lack of spot yarn, long positions showed good interest. Some said that Japanese yarn could yield a profit of about twenty-five yuan per piece based on the cost of raw cotton and were very willing to open positions on far-term contracts, but yarn merchants were temporarily hesitant to accept them. Changyu, Wang Taixing, Gengfeng, Yongchang, and others sold off, while Taichang, Shenji, Yichang, Fukang, and others bought in. Volume was not strong. As a result, spot yarn prices for each month fell by two to six jiao compared to the previous day's close. When the market opened in the afternoon, the market sentiment was calm. There was no major trading in the second session. Unexpectedly, a surge in prices suddenly occurred in the third session, causing an urgent situation. It was said that there were about 3,000 bales of 20-count Samsung yarn available this month. The Tianjin gang bought 500 bales of this bargaining chip, and negotiations were underway for the rest. Also, the selling price was very high, so short sellers rushed to cover their positions, causing prices to jump. In short, the spot goods are too scarce, so the price is likely to rise easily but not fall. The close for October was 218 yuan. As a result, each month's price rose by two yuan six jiao to three yuan three jiao compared to the morning close. Cotton Also Pushes Towards New Heights; However, Due to Large-Scale Selling by Major Players, the Rise is Not as Strong as in the Yarn Market 105

The cotton market was weak in the morning but rose sharply in the afternoon, and the momentum is also pushing towards new heights. However, the major players are currently selling in bulk. However, the selling prices in various regions are difficult to loosen, and the price difference between yarn and cotton is too large given that yarn prices are constantly hitting new highs, so a reaction will be inevitable later on.

Today's weather forecast predicts clouds or light rain in the east, and slight clouds in the central and western regions. The close was flat and weak, with spot goods rising eight pounds and futures rising two to eight pounds. British cotton spot goods rose ten points, and futures rose eight to ten points. Blue cloth yuan twill also rose in price, but not as quickly as unbleached piece goods. Due to the lack of gray fabric, the output of printed goods and finished fabrics has been reduced, and the daily sales are extremely good.

Northeast soybeans, this year's harvest is said to be only about 70%, causing costs to increase. Trading for profit is not easy. Approximately 1,200 packages were traded in total.

Finance: Gold Standard Forward Fluctuations, Large Players' Selling Intentions Remain Strong, Resulting in a Further Drop of 70 Cents 116

Although spot gold prices rose yesterday, stability was only slightly evident off-exchange. Large players increased their short positions and closed out long positions, leading to a downstream trend. The future market's fluctuations depended on forward premiums. Initial morning reports indicated stable or slightly higher forward silver prices in overseas silver markets, including London, New York, and Montreal, with exchange rates decreasing. London spot gold rose by one penny. The Central Bank's official exchange rate announcement showed no change for both London and New York, while customs gold units increased by two percent. The standard gold price was quoted at 1,154.70 yuan, with pre-market trading opening at 1,152.50 yuan or higher. Ding Kang Heng Yu sold off, falling back within two yuan. The morning opened lower. Although there was a brief rally after the opening, large players increased their short positions, and some long players also entered late. Buyers were hesitant. The HSBC exchange rate announcement showed no change for both London and New York, and the silver equalization tax remained unchanged. With a lack of changes mid-day, the trend weakened. Large players bought in at the lows, providing some support, and the market gradually stabilized by noon. Later, the market slightly weakened, but recovered as forward premiums fell, boosting confidence. However, the gains were limited as large players took profits, and the rising forward premiums pushed the market downstream again. In the end, the situation was uncertain. Yesterday, forwards were quoted at a premium of around 2.50 yuan by long players. The day's market conditions are recorded below:

The morning opening was at 1,151.70 yuan, a drop of ten cents from the previous close. Hong Chang Yong bought a large position, pushing the price up to 1,152.10 yuan. Da De Cheng Yuan Mao Yong sold off, falling back to 1,151.60 yuan. Cheng Da Shang bought. HSBC's official exchange rate announcement showed no change for both London and New York, and the price rose to 1,151.80 yuan. Yuan Mao Yong and Da De Cheng continued to sell, and the silver equalization tax announcement showed no change, falling back to 1,150.60 yuan. Cheng Da, Da Chang Xiang, Fu Xing Yong, Qia Feng Yong, and other firms maintained their positions by buying on the dips. The noon close was at 1,151.40 yuan.

The afternoon opening was at 1,151.30 yuan. Yuan Mao Yong, Heng Yu, and Cheng Da sold, bringing the price down to 1,151.10 yuan. Fu Xing Yong, Qia Feng Yong, and Cheng Da bought back, and forward premiums fell from 2.50 yuan to 2.00 yuan, then rose to 2.30 yuan. Qia Feng Yong, Fu Xing Yong, Heng Chang Yong, Sheng Yuan Yong, and other firms sold off, and forward premiums rose again to 2.50-2.60 yuan, then gradually fell to 1.00 yuan. Da De Cheng Lai Jin briefly rose to 1.80 yuan, while Heng Chang Yong sold off, pushing the price back down to 1.00 yuan. After fluctuating, the closing price was 1,151.10 yuan. After the close, Da De Cheng, Fu Yu, and Yu Gou bought, providing more stability.

The closing price, based on the Central Bank's standard gold price, rose to 1,154.70 yuan. According to the spot market price, the spot price was over one yuan higher. The registration price for this month was 1,146 yuan, and for November it was 1,151 yuan. The morning water price was 1,146 yuan. The spot market was stable. Da De Cheng, Tong Feng, Heng Jing, Fu Shen, Da Yong, Yuan Mao Yong, Zheng Chang, Tong Tai Chang, Heng Yu, Ding Kang, Heng Chang Yong, and others were among the sellers. Da De Cheng bought after selling. Cheng Da, Chun Yuan Yong, Qia Feng Yong, and Sheng Yuan Yong bought first and then sold.

The day's market still saw mixed activity. The morning opening was at 1,151.70 yuan, and the closing was at 1,151.10 yuan. The high was 1,152.30 yuan, and the low was 1,150.60 yuan, a fluctuation of 1.70 yuan. As a result, the price fell by 70 cents from the previous close.

After the opening, although Yuan Chang Yong, Da De Cheng, and Jing Fu bought, Heng Chang Yong, Yuan Mao Yong, Fu Xing Yong, Yi Da, Ding Kang, and Shun Li sold, pushing the price up to 2.60 yuan. After the close, although Qing Fa Yong and Cheng Da bought, Da Chang Xiang sold and remained stable.

On Reading, to My Nephew 121

— Xie Si

Xi Cong:

I received your letter and learned that you passed your transfer exam. I was very happy to hear that. You said, "From now on, I can walk less each day and save the time I spend walking to read more books." These two sentences are correct, but reading is not a casual matter. It's not just about burying yourself in books all the time. Your grandfather's letter says that you only like to read novels. As long as you have a novel in hand, you lie on the rattan chair all day and even forget to eat. Although I don't object to young people reading novels, I don't think this method is right. Reading is like eating. After you eat something, you need your stomach to be able to digest it and digest it cleanly. "Indigestion" and "gluttony" will ruin your stomach, that's one point; secondly, if you don't pick and choose what you eat, you'll also ruin your stomach. The ancients said, "Sickness enters through the mouth," which is because you don't pick and choose what you eat. Reading is the same. Burying yourself in books all day will cause your brain to become congested, and soon your brain will become dizzy. This is very dangerous for your body. And with your reading method, you definitely can't fully understand the meaning of the book - at most you only understand the story recorded in the book, which is also wrong. When young people read, on the one hand, they should understand the content of the book, but the most important thing is to understand and analyze the methods used by others to write articles. Because when we read, on the one hand, we are seeking knowledge, and on the other hand, we are gaining methods for writing articles by others as a reference for when we write our own articles. If you don't add criticism or taste the method when reading, you will never be able to write your own articles, and you will never be able to use pen and ink to convey your thoughts to the world. What's the point of reading like that? Reading like that, even if you read for a lifetime, even if you finish reading all the books in front of you, even if you remember them all, aren't you just like a bookshelf? As a joke, a bookshelf can still be burned as firewood, but a bookworm who has read books and can't express them is useless except for eating.

Most importantly, there is so-called "food poisoning," and there is also poison in the books you read. If you don't choose carefully, there is also a risk of brain poisoning. I hope you will ask your teacher more about this. If your teacher has already given you a list of books you should read, that's great. If not, you can either ask your teacher to make a list, or you can first ask your teacher to review the books you want to read. If the teacher says it's okay, then read it carefully. That way, you may be able to avoid the danger of brain poisoning!

Writing this, I want to talk to you about my bad experiences reading in the past. I started school later than you. At your age, I was still in elementary school, but my physical and mental development was similar to yours. What I liked at that time was also novels. At that time, the school teacher prohibited students from reading novels, but the stories in novels were more interesting than the things in textbooks, and besides the Chinese, arithmetic, English, history, geography, and science classes that needed to be reviewed a little, there was a lot of free time every day. I didn't like to exercise - and the school didn't force us to exercise either, so several of us classmates adopted the method of secretly reading novels to pass our extra time. I was living at the school at that time, and I didn't want to go home even on holidays, because I could hide in the dormitory and read novels all day long. On weekdays, I put the novel by the bedside. As soon as the sky was a little bit white, I would take the small lamp from the bedside and read greedily. When I was in self-study class, I would also put the novel under the textbook. As soon as the teacher's footsteps left, my hand would close the textbook, and my eyes would simultaneously focus on the oily paper and small print below. Even the ten or twenty minutes before going to bed and turning off the vegetable oil lamp were not spared. I would rather fumble in the dark to take off my clothes after turning off the light.

What did the three years I spent in late elementary school - what was then called higher elementary school - give to my body and mind?

First, it made my eyes nearsighted: because those novels were all lithographic prints as large as the current font size 5, plus the reflection of the oily paper. The light of the vegetable oil lamp at night and the fish-white light of the morning were both utilized through the coarse yellow calico curtain, and I had to press the book against my nose. At first, I felt my eyeballs swell, and later I had to sit in the first or second row to see the words on the blackboard. When I entered middle school, I finally couldn't do without wearing glasses.

Second, it cultivated my neurasthenia and insomnia: the dormitory didn't have self-study room equipment, and I mostly read novels lying in bed, so the blood gathered smoothly in my head. At first I felt my face was hot, then I felt my brain was swelling. Although my brain was extremely tired, I couldn't help but think, "I don't know how it will turn out, let's listen to the next chapter." With one stroke, oh, did he die in the end? So I couldn't care about whether my brain was tired or not. And even if I had to put it down, the stories in the novel, even though they didn't concern me, I couldn't help but think about them one by one. Not only did I think with my eyes open, but I couldn't help but have many nightmares or erotic dreams with my eyes closed. In this way, at first I didn't want to sleep, and later I couldn't sleep even if I wanted to. Later I realized that this was "insomnia," this was so-called neurasthenia!

Third, it made me develop the bad habit of "swallowing dates whole" when reading: reading novels only pays attention to the story, and that's how most young people are, right? And what I read at that time were all chaptered novels, such as Tang Chuan, Zheng Dong, Zheng Xi, Seven Heroes and Five Justices, Water Margin, Ji Gong Zhuan, Jing Hua Yuan, etc. Of course, there were also things that were concisely described, but the textbooks used by the storytellers had many typos and broken sentences, and there were also many long, dry vegetable-like sandwiched articles. So, in order to quickly know the content of the story, on the one hand, I had to adopt the "kill the robbers" principle for the unfamiliar words in the book - for example, "咱" and "喒" I would read them as "自" and "咎" and read them like that for three years - on the other hand, I had to adopt the "running horse policy" and quickly skim over the descriptions in the story that I thought were unimportant. As a result, the way I read novels was like this, and when I read non-fiction, I couldn't help but do the same. I remember that we read three volumes of English at that time. The unfamiliar words in the first two volumes could be recited in order from the first word on the first page to the last page, but the unfamiliar words in the third volume could not only not be recited, but even the pronunciation could not be spelled to seventy or eighty percent. I could only know a vague general idea of ​​the books I read, and I could never answer clearly when asked about the content.

Fourth, it caused irreparable damage to my body: Many of the descriptions in the novels I read were extremely bad, and there were many explicit and implicit hints that urged premature maturity, making me, as a young man, feel as sore in my waist and legs as an old man. When I think about it now, I can't help but feel pain and regret. The danger of indiscriminately reading without selection is more terrible than poisonous snakes and beasts for young people who have unstable minds and strong curiosity.

Xi Cong, I am still afraid when I think back to my situation in elementary school. In a word, I hope you will not follow in my footsteps!

The above words are my thoughts and bad experiences. Now I will talk to you about reading methods from a positive aspect.

The purpose of reading is firstly to seek knowledge, and secondly to tell others what you know. Seeking knowledge is to seek clear and clear knowledge. In other words, the books you read must be completely understood. After understanding, you should add criticism based on the knowledge you have gained elsewhere. Some people say that the criticism of those who lack knowledge - even if it refers to a junior high school student like you - is incorrect. Incorrect criticism is still better than no criticism. In fact, this logic is wrong: we must know that there is no end to knowledge. If middle school students cannot criticize, then how can college students be considered capable of criticism in the eyes of scholars? Even those who are recognized as so-called scholars, in the endless progress of science, can they always make unchanging criticisms? Criticism is the axe that forges knowledge. The more you know, the more accurate your criticism will be. Constantly seeking knowledge and constantly criticizing is the way to read. Just seeking knowledge without making expressions, as mentioned above, is the reading method of a useless bookworm. Although the expression may not necessarily be a mature thought, if you don't practice the ability to express, even when your thoughts are mature, you will not be able to use skillful methods to express them.

Based on this simple principle, whenever you read an article or a book, you must first pay attention to two points: first, what is the structure of the article? Second, what is the idea of ​​the article? You must analyze and review it carefully. Therefore, you must prepare a reading notebook. After reading, you must make a report. Although this report is not necessarily for anyone to see, after a while, you can know whether these reports are correct or wrong, because your planned reading will definitely gradually increase your knowledge and make your criticism more accurate.

Preface to "A Collection of Cool Songs" 122

— Xia Gai Zun

When Venerable Hongyi had not yet become a monk, he excelled in all artistic endeavors. He was uniquely accomplished in calligraphy, painting, music, literature, drama, and seal carving. He once told me that he had worked the hardest on music throughout his life, as musical theory and performance cannot be mastered without long-term practice, unlike other artistic pursuits that can rely on talent. The Venerable taught music in Hangzhou and Nanjing for ten years, and today, nineteen music teachers across the country are his disciples. His compositions and songs are popular throughout the country and are considered masterpieces. After entering the mountains, all previous pursuits became a dream. One day, Liu Zhiping and I visited the Venerable at a mountain temple. After lunch, we chatted casually and touched upon contemporary music education. Zhiping sighed at the difficulty of finding songwriters, lamenting the prevalence of vulgar songs in the streets and alleys, and deeply regretting the Venerable's early entry into the mountains. The Venerable was also moved and agreed to write more songs, which surprised and delighted Zhiping and me. This happened seven years ago. In the past seven years, Zhiping and his fellow students have composed music for the Venerable's lyrics, carefully refining them until they were approved by the Venerable. After performances at the Shanghai Former Xinhua Art School and the Zhejiang Ningbo Middle School, they brought the manuscript to me, seeking publication. There are five composers: Zhiping is the Venerable's disciple; Xue Yong, Xi Yi, and Bo Ying are Zhiping's disciples; and Xu Tang is Zhiping's great-grandson. All are outstanding figures in the field of music education. There are only five songs, but they are the result of collaborative efforts between teachers and disciples in the music world, spanning seven years. This is also a remarkable story in Chinese music history. The song is named "Coolness," as the Venerable commanded. The Venerable's lay surname is Li, his given name is Xi, his courtesy name is Shutong, and another courtesy name is Xishuang. He is from Pinghu, Zhejiang.

"Extinction" Seventh Edition Postscript 123

— Ba Jin

"Extinction" is my first published work, written in 1928. Now, eight years have passed. Recently, taking advantage of the seventh edition, I read it carefully, deleted and revised many parts, and handed it to the bookstore for a revised and reset edition. I had the idea to revise this book three or four years ago, but other things entangled me, preventing me from fulfilling my wish. Today, after reading the proofs sent by the bookstore, I feel very happy, feeling as if I have finally accomplished something.

However, at the same time, other thoughts arose in me. I seemed to have returned to the time when I was writing this book. Regarding the motivation and process of writing this book, I have described it in detail in my article "A Review of My Writing Life." This article has been included in my first collection of short stories, so it is not convenient to include it here. I also wrote a diary at that time, but it was lost in the January 28th Incident. I also wrote an "Author's Confession of Extinction," which was a response to some critics. There was a large passage in it describing my attitude when creating the typical character of Du Daxin, which I feel can be quoted here:

"When I wrote about Du Daxin's thoughts, I adopted a completely objective attitude and did not completely infuse my own thoughts into it. Although I am not a believer in Du Daxin, I love him, and my attitude towards him is very fair. I wrote about his strengths, but I also wrote about his weaknesses. However, the criticism from Mr. Gang Goren is somewhat unfair. He said that Du Daxin's 'motivation for participating in the revolution is incorrect. He uses work to suppress his depression and uses the revolution to express his personal ideals.' I admit that Du Daxin 'is a romantic revolutionary,' which is true, but to say that his motivation for participating in the revolution is incorrect is too unfair to him. The reason why he became a romantic revolutionary and the reason why he hated humanity are due to his environment and his lung disease. 'What a despicable thing man is!' If Du Daxin had said this sentence like Sanin, he would have the right to do so. His participation in the revolution is one thing, and his use of work to suppress his depression is another. It is not because he wants to suppress his depression that he participates in the revolution. Man is a complex, organic thing, and people with lung disease are even more sensitive. After participating in the revolution, he cannot become a machine. His environment still makes him depressed, but he does not become disillusioned or give up everything. Of course, he can only use work to suppress his depression. I myself once received a letter from a friend in China who said that he was in great pain and was 'using busyness as intoxication.' Isn't this the same as Du Daxin? As for Du Daxin's death, I think it is inevitable. Mr. Gang said, 'Sacrificing one's own life and seeking revenge merely because a friend's friend was killed... is not the attitude that a revolutionary should have.' However, if Mr. Gang thinks more deeply, he will definitely understand that Du Daxin only had one path in front of him: death. A person who hates humanity and hates himself will either kill or be killed, or commit suicide. In my opinion, he has no third option, especially since Du Daxin also has lung disease. Revenge is a minor matter. The most important thing is that his advanced lung disease made 'him begin to feel that this long-lasting suffering should stop. He wants to rest, he wants to rest permanently.' And in fact, for him, 'only death can bring him peaceful happiness' (page 330). The Russian politician Radek had a classmate in his youth who contracted an incurable disease. That person asked Radek to poison him with poison, but Radek did not agree. However, he wrote in his diary: 'Life that cannot be tolerated should be destroyed with violence.' He himself later committed suicide. Du Daxin 'knows that he is working hard to walk towards the road to death, and he clearly feels that death is approaching day by day.' Of course, he will take the path of destroying life with violence. I myself am against him taking this path, but I cannot stop him. I can only cry for his death."

On the first page of the first edition of "Extinction," I printed a dedication. I dedicated this book to my eldest brother, who was the first person who gave me the greatest help in my intellectual development. Now I have deleted this short dedication because my brother has left this world. I wrote this book for him to read in order to seek his understanding and let me go my own way with peace of mind. However, we finally separated forever without understanding each other.

I repeatedly flipped through the pages of the proofs in front of me, trying to find something on these glossy pages. I am afraid of recalling, but now I desperately seek help from recalling.

The cold wind of late spring blows in from the window. The surroundings are silent. The night is very late. What is the use of sitting alone in front of the window and writing articles? Can't I do something more useful?

Introduction to Two Readable Books 124

— Ai Ji

... The Story of Chemistry and The Story of Arithmetic ...

Everyone knows that chemistry is one of the modern sciences, and at the same time, everyone admits that it was not produced out of thin air or by chance. But if asked about the state of chemistry around a certain century? Who were the chemists at that time? What memorable contributions did they make? And how did his contribution come about? Not everyone can answer that. For example, who discovered gases such as hydrogen, oxygen, nitrogen, and chlorine? Which year was it discovered? What were the detailed processes and methods of discovery? These are all very valuable questions. But this can only be understood by those who have read the history of chemistry, I'm afraid no one can understand. Also, how did Cavendish discover nitric acid from the air? How did Dalton measure atomic weight? How did structural theory sprout? How did the concept of electrons and atomic structure arise? This is only possible in the history of chemistry, and it is definitely not a rigid chemistry textbook that can comprehensively and systematically tell us.

Speaking of textbooks, they can sometimes guide students to study various subjects, but sometimes they are also a major obstacle for students to study various subjects. Because its content is restricted by curriculum standards and other aspects, it is often just fragments of dead knowledge, not systematic and living knowledge.

Now, in order to enable general young students to gain systematic and lively knowledge of chemistry, I would like to introduce "The Story of Chemistry" (Kaiming Edition, priced at 55 cents) written by Japanese writer Masuyo Kura and translated by Ren Yibi. This is a concise history of chemistry with wonderful and essential content and fluent and smooth translation. It was also produced because the author was dissatisfied with school textbooks. This can be seen from a paragraph in the author's preface below:

"When I was teaching chemistry and physics at a normal school, I had a deep dissatisfaction with the textbooks... Students' interest in subjects is mostly in the hands of teachers, but now the textbooks seem to be restraining the teacher's skills. ... Chemistry is originally an interesting subject, but according to the content of the current textbooks, it is definitely impossible to satisfy students. To remedy this deficiency, it is indeed necessary to talk about the history of chemistry from a position different from that of the textbooks and in a way that has nothing to do with it.

The above is the purpose and position of the book. Now, let me briefly introduce its content: This book is divided into two parts, the former and the latter. The former part mainly describes Lavoisier and his era, while the latter part describes the era after Lavoisier. Before Lavoisier, chemistry was always in the barren burning flame of darkness, and could not get the illumination of light. Until the time of Lavoisier, he boldly overthrew the phlogiston theory that had dominated chemistry for hundreds of years. From then on, chemistry saw the light of day and developed from morning to the present state. Therefore, the author divides the history of chemistry into two periods. The former part has four chapters. The first chapter is "The Pioneers of Chemistry: Alchemy," which explains that chemistry originated from alchemy and gradually developed with the progress of alchemy. The second chapter is "Before Boyle," which explains the development of chemistry before Boyle and in his time. The third chapter is "The Theory of Combustion," which explains how the thoughts of chemists in the 100 years after Boyle were dominated by the absurd phlogiston theory and the process by which Schule and Priestley discovered oxygen. The fourth chapter is "The Construction of Modern Chemistry," which talks about Lavoisier's overthrow of the phlogiston theory and the contributions of other chemists of the same era to chemistry. The latter part is divided into eight chapters, namely "Davy and his Disciples," "The Development of Atomic and Molecular Theory," "The Origin of Element Symbols and Chemical Formulas," "Element Discovery and the Periodic Law," "The Past and Present of Solution Theory," "The Emergence of Ionization Theory," "The Size of Atoms and Molecules," and "The Chemical Revolution." We only need to read these eight chapters to systematically know the general course of chemistry from Lavoisier to the present.

In addition to all the wonderful content mentioned above, this book also contains several characteristics, which we should bring up and talk about: First, the content of general chemistry textbooks is selected based on the presence or absence of the results of chemists' experiments. Therefore, whether theoretically or experimentally, anything without results, or with poor results, or results that are contrary to common rules, is often discarded and not discussed. But in this book, both process and results are equally important, so it does not judge people by success or failure, and can allow readers to see the clues of the changes in chemical thought and observation. Second, people who compile ordinary chemistry textbooks often compile the many results created by chemists over hundreds or even thousands of years without any connection due to unavoidable reasons, trying to stuff these indigestible things into the brains of scholars, regardless of whether they will be digested or not, making chemistry a very unnatural machine. The compilation of this book does not have the above shortcomings. It definitely does not want us to force ourselves to memorize those stereotypical facts. Third, it can show us that chemistry is endless, and guide us to a broad road, teaching us to work hard to explore the treasure trove contained in chemistry. That's why I dare to introduce this book.

Next, let's talk about "The Story of Arithmetic" (Kaiming Edition, priced at 65 cents).

If we ask middle school students, "Do you like arithmetic?" then perhaps seven or eight out of ten of them will answer: "I don't like it very much," or some people will say: "I find it quite annoying." Since the college entrance examination system was established, arithmetic is probably also the subject with the most failing students. "Is arithmetic really a hateful subject? Why is it not easy to get close to people? Why is it not liked? Is there a way to remedy it? I can't help but have such questions.

"The pure abstractness of arithmetic is the most difficult to understand. The reason why most people dislike arithmetic and say that arithmetic is not easy to understand is probably at this point. And the arithmetic professors of the past have also focused on this point, so it will create a situation where people get more and more confused. Someone defines arithmetic as, if you don't ask what it is, you still understand, but if you ask what it is, you get more and more confused; this is to bring out the abstractness of arithmetic. For ordinary people, it is too abstract and indeed not easy to understand.

"However, does it have to be so abstract to be considered arithmetic? In shallow places, in practical social life, do we not often have arithmetic problems? Why must we learn the abstract and difficult-to-understand arithmetic in the books? This is where the failure of arithmetic education has always been. Ordinary people do not require such profound and abstract arithmetic, but those who teach arithmetic refuse to use concrete things to represent abstract things and give a clear reality. Thus, arithmetic has become an incomprehensible and difficult-to-understand subject that is disliked by people."

The above are two paragraphs from the preface of "The Story of Arithmetic" written by Mr. Zhang Kebiao. From this, we can know that arithmetic is not born to be hated by people and not easy to get close to. The reason is only that people do not know how to use it and study it well.

Recently, many people often use lively and lively writing styles to write arithmetic essays. For example, Mr. Liu Xunyu's "Mathematics Garden" and "Mathematical Fun." This kind of writing can very well arouse students' interest in studying arithmetic. This is indeed a good way to remedy the deficiencies of general arithmetic textbooks.

No matter what kind of homework you study, if you want to achieve twice the result with half the effort, then the method of research must first be from combination to division, and finally from division to combination; in other words, you must first use the method of induction to obtain all the important outlines of a certain subject, and then use the method of deduction to expand it, and finally use the method of induction to synthesize the various more broad and true knowledge. Only this kind of learning method can make the subject clear and easy to understand. The method of learning arithmetic should also be like this. You should first get a concept of the whole arithmetic, and then you can study it step by step. This book "The Story of Arithmetic" was produced in response to such a need. Please see what Mr. Zhang said: "This book is for young people to read outside of class. It seeks to be shallow and easy to understand, so it does not talk about arithmetic principles... It only pays attention to the general situation of its development... My humble intention is to increase the interest in arithmetic to some extent through this, and give a little nourishment to this dry and tasteless subject of arithmetic, so that arithmetic will not be regarded as an annoying subject."

Its compilation is like this: It takes the path of development of arithmetic as the backbone, and records the anecdotes and deeds of various famous mathematicians from ancient times to modern times, as well as the contributions of each person to arithmetic. It says very little about formal arithmetic principles, but it also pays attention to the causal relationship of how science rises and how it declines. Also, although it only records various characters on the surface, in essence, we can see the cultural and political background of that era, which is another characteristic of this book.

Page 13

Local News

General Situation of Salt Administration Consolidation Since the Establishment of the National Government; Audit Agencies Concurrently Handle Anti-Smuggling Affairs; Unified Authority; Balanced Tax Rates; Increased Tax Revenue; Foreign Debts Can Be Cleared 125

According to the Central News Agency, there have been many changes in China's salt administration, and the content is very complicated. Few people can thoroughly understand it. Since the Legislative Yuan passed the new salt law and the National Government promulgated it, how the new law is implemented and how the authorities have consolidated it in recent years have attracted the attention of society. A reporter specially visited a senior official of the Salt Administration Audit Office of the Ministry of Finance to ask about the consolidation of the salt administration and tax revenue since the establishment of the National Government. He provided a very detailed account, which is recorded as follows:

Improving Organization

China's salt administration organization has separated administration and audit since 1923. The reason for this construction is that the audit agency is not without foreign debt contracts. However, since the establishment of the National Government, this restriction has been lifted, and it has always been enthusiastic and successful in consolidating the salt administration and rectifying tax revenue. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance has successively transferred the administrative and anti-smuggling affairs of the eleven regions of Huaibei, Huainan, Zhe, Su, Lu, Min, Yu, Xiang, E, Xi, and Wan to Chinese auditors of the audit office for concurrent management in 1931 and 1932. Later, it was ordered by the Ministry to transfer the administrative and anti-smuggling agencies of Changlu, Northwest, and Sichuan to the audit agency for concurrent management, so as to unify authority and facilitate improvement. Although the concurrent management has not been long, the consolidation has achieved considerable results. In recent years, the progress of the consolidation of the salt administration and the obvious achievements are roughly as follows:

Consolidating Anti-Smuggling Affairs

In the past, the malpractices of anti-smuggling were mostly in embezzlement, sale of posts, release of private goods, extortion, etc. Since the audit office received the anti-smuggling agencies of the eleven regions such as Huaibei, it reorganized the anti-smuggling camp into tax police, eliminating the weak and retaining the strong, and strictly training them. All appointments and dismissals of officials and police were handled in accordance with the personnel management regulations of the audit office to ensure job security, and independent military supplies were implemented, with roll calls and payments made. Clothing, firearms, and ammunition were also purchased and distributed by the audit office through bidding. The past malpractices were swept away. In recent years, the increase in the number of domestic sales of salt in these regions is indeed not as good as in other regions that have not been concurrently managed.

Consolidating Salt Fields

China's salt fields have never been managed properly, so smuggling is easy, and the loss of salt tax amounts to tens of millions of yuan every year. After the establishment of the Salt Administration Audit Office, the Changlu Guantuo was built. In recent years, enclosing walls, trenches, and roads have been added, and tax police outposts and field affairs offices have been set up in the field, so that in addition to storing salt, the beach production, transportation, and prevention of beach smuggling can be managed at the same time. In the past five years, various projects in Huaibei Tantuo have also been gradually equipped, beach smuggling has been sharply reduced, and Lu, Zhe, Su, and Min are also under construction. In the future, when various projects are completed, beach smuggling will be eliminated, and tax revenue will naturally increase.

Improving Transportation and Sales

For example, the wheel sales system on the four banks of the Yangtze River is the main reason for the sluggish sales of official salt. Now, restricted free trade is gradually being promoted as a preliminary step towards abolition, and Huai salt on the four banks, whether in the field or on the bank, is allowed to freely reduce prices within the statutory price to compete for sales. Transportation is also encouraged to save transportation costs. In addition, the franchise merchants in the two prefectures of Wenzhou and Chu in eastern Zhejiang and the three prefectures of Yanjian and Shao in Fujian have been abolished, and free trade has been implemented. Nanjing City and the four counties of Lintan, Fei, and Yi in Shandong have been opened as free trade zones to prepare for the implementation of the new salt law.

Suppressing Niter Salt

In the regions of Ji, Lu, and Yu, the loss of tax revenue due to the encroachment of niter soil salt each year amounts to more than 30 million yuan. In 1932, the Niter and Sulfur Bureaus of various provinces were merged into the audit office. By 1935, the income from niter and sulfur had increased more than fourfold. The niter salt produced from niter production is now generally dumped to prevent smuggling of salt for food. In the Changlu area, the local officials and fair gentry are also jointly advising the people to destroy the soil salt ponds, and at the same time, water conservancy is being carried out to change the soil quality and eliminate soil salt. The tax revenue in the district in 1935 increased by more than 3 million yuan compared with 1934. In Henan, the government allocated funds to jointly manage waterways and improve soil with the provincial authorities, and set up an agricultural experiment field to improve alkaline soil. The results were very significant. The most difficult problem of niter soil salt in the salt administration for thousands of years is expected to be solved.

Balanced Tax Rates

The salt tax rates were reorganized by the audit office after its establishment in 1913, and once tended to be tidy. Later, the country was in turmoil, the political situation was unstable, and the local governments took the lead in arbitrarily adding surcharges, resulting in different weights in each region. After the establishment of the National Government, it made great efforts to consolidate, first unifying the tax days and merging the various confusing and complicated names into categories. The field tax and central surtax paid in the producing area are collectively named the positive tax, and the bank tax and central surtax paid in the selling area are collectively named the sales tax. Later, the Ministry of Finance issued an order in 1933 stipulating that from January 1, 1934, all central positive and surtaxes and local surtaxes totaling more than 10 yuan per load should be reduced to 10 yuan uniformly. Those below 10 yuan should wait for consideration of the situation before gradually improving to equalize the burden. At present, the tax rates in each region have gradually become balanced, and all the long-standing bad rules have been fundamentally eliminated in recent years.

Increased Tax Revenue

The tax revenue in 1924 was more than 75 million yuan, which gradually increased over the years. By 1935, it was more than 183 million yuan, which can be attributed to the effectiveness of the audit office's concurrent management of administration and anti-smuggling. For example, in the fifteen years from 1914 to 1928, the total average tax revenue of the eleven regions such as Huaibei, which were concurrently managing administration and anti-smuggling, and the nine regions such as Guangdong, which were not concurrently managing, was more than 35 million yuan. By 1933, the former was more than 114 million yuan, and the latter was only 45 million yuan, a difference of as much as 70 million yuan. After 1933, due to the inclusion of the Changlu and Koubei districts, the former was more than 146 million yuan, and the latter was only more than 36 million yuan. The salt administration expenses have been reduced by 3.5 million yuan per year since the concurrent management of administration and anti-smuggling. In recent years, although the duties of the audit agency have increased, the expenses have been reduced as much as possible. The budget for administrative expenses in 1935 was less than 5% of the tax revenue, while the increase in police in anti-smuggling and the purchase of firearms were higher than before.

Reduced Foreign Debt

After 1913, the salt tax was originally the sole guarantee for the post-war large loan, and this led to the gradual interference of foreigners in the salt administration. After the establishment of the National Government, in addition to maintaining national sovereignty and reforming the management of the audit office, all foreign debt matters were under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Finance, and the audit office only managed tax revenue. The guarantee for the post-war loan was transferred to the customs revenue item to earn salt tax and enrich the national use. At present, the foreign debts guaranteed by salt tax are only the British-French loan, the Crisp loan, and the Hubei-Guangdong loan, which can be repaid separately within a few years. In summary, the progress of China's salt administration since the establishment of the National Government has been rapid, and the achievements have been remarkable, which was unprecedented before. At present, the Legislative Yuan has adopted a one-yuan system for the salt administration organization, which is in line with political principles. If this consistent spirit is followed and the same consolidation is carried out in all regions of the country, the results will be even more impressive.

Banking Sector Agrees to Handle National Rice Transportation Loans; The Amount Should Be Determined Next Week; Grain Merchants Very Much Hope for Unified Cooperation 126

According to the Central News Agency, this year's national rice harvest is abundant. In order to prevent the decline in grain prices from harming farmers, the government has ordered the banking sector to earnestly handle transportation loans to provide relief. It is reported that the banks are now negotiating to handle it collectively. Grain merchants also hope that the government and the banking sector will cooperate and coordinate. The details are recorded below:

Unstable Market Prices

In recent days, the market for miscellaneous grains has been fluctuating, and the rise and fall are unpredictable. The reason is nothing more than the influence of foreign merchants and gardeners' monopoly. However, normal merchants still hope that the government authorities will take effective measures to stabilize market prices and ensure people's food supply. According to inquiries from grain merchants, the fluctuation of miscellaneous grains this time is not caused by the normal supply relationship. For example, the price of rice soared by more than one yuan a few days ago, and then dropped by more than one yuan recently. In addition, the prices of flour and wheat have been rising sharply together, but recently the price of wheat is still rising, while the price of flour has fallen. This is indeed a rare and abnormal development in the food market.

Earnestly Unified Measures

It was further stated that in this extraordinary period, there are earnest and unified measures in both production and transportation. This is what our legitimate grain merchants are eagerly hoping for. At present, the National Economic Commission and the Ministry of Finance and Finance are both paying close attention to the matter of grain and are gradually promoting it. The banking group is also gradually increasing the amount of loans released to rural areas. However, this matter should eventually have an earnest and unified method. Whether it is in transportation or production, there should be close contact. If the government and merchants can cooperate, the effect will be greater. In the future, it is hoped that the government and grain merchants will cooperate in transportation, and the government and the banking sector will cooperate in production loans. Everything will still be planned by the government in a unified manner, which can avoid the monopoly of foreign merchants and prevent the manipulation of unscrupulous merchants. If so, the food market can be stabilized and the future of the people's food supply can be optimistic.

Banking Sector Attaches Great Importance

The banks in the city have received orders from the Ministry of Finance to handle national rice transportation loans as much as possible to develop rural areas and regulate the people's food supply. According to the reporter's investigation, the banking sector attaches great importance to this. Previously, the Bank of China and the Shanghai Bank suggested centralized handling, which was approved by the banks. More than ten banks gathered responsible persons in the Bank of China on the 15th to discuss. The principle of centralized handling of national rice transportation loans has been approved, and the loan interest rate is generally reduced as much as possible to benefit farmers and merchants. The specific methods are being studied. It is heard that another meeting will be convened next week to determine the loan amount.

Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed Request for Clarification: Start Date for Taxing Business Profits 127

Yesterday, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance requesting clarification on the starting date for taxing business profits. The original petition stated: Regarding the matter of submitting a request, it is noted that on the 14th of this month, a letter from Changming Electric Company stated that, upon investigation of Article 1, Clause 1 of the Income Tax Regulations, Category 1 covers income from businesses, commercial firms, shops, and factories, or individual capital exceeding 2,000 yuan; furthermore, according to the Ministry of Finance's directive, Categories 1, 2, and 3, and all other income types, are to be taxed starting from January 1, 1937. Moreover, Rule 26 of the Detailed Rules for Implementing Income Tax stipulates that the tax payment deadline for both Categories A and B should be based on each industry's annual settlement period. Investigations reveal that each industry's annual settlement period varies, with some in June and others in December. For those in June, the shareholders' meeting is invariably held in August or September; for those in December, the shareholders' meeting is invariably held in March or April of the following year. While there is no issue for commercial firms that traditionally distribute dividends at the end of the year, companies organized according to company law must distribute dividends only after the shareholders' meeting, if there is a surplus. Now, the income tax for Category 1, Item A, and Category 3 (stock dividends) is to be levied from January 1, 1937. For companies settling accounts in December, the dividend distribution period is indeed after the tax start date, but the actual income is from profits earned before the end of December 1936. Laws should not be retroactive. Therefore, all companies settling accounts in December 1936 should not be required to pay income tax uniformly. For those with a settlement period in June of the following year, income tax should be levied for six months of income from 1937. Furthermore, the income tax on interest from deposits was originally scheduled to start on October 1st of this year. According to the Ministry of Finance's order, the interest income earned before October 1st is still to be fully distributed and exempt from taxation. Thus, the situation is the same for Category 1, Item A (business profits), and Category 3 (stock dividends). The Ministry's order to start taxation from January 1, 1937, must mean that only income earned after January 1st should be taxed. It should be stipulated that business profits and stock dividends earned before December 31, 1936, are exempt from taxation, which is in line with legal principles and factual circumstances. With the end of the year approaching, it is easy to cause misunderstandings when companies settle accounts. Therefore, we offer our opinion and request that your association submit this matter for discussion, present it to the Ministry of Finance, and announce a clear method that aligns with legal principles and reflects reality. Upon arrival at the meeting, it was noted that, apart from civil servant salaries and securities interest, all other income taxes are to be levied from January 1, 1937, as per the Ministry's general order. The meaning of starting taxation from January 1st should refer to the taxation of income earned from January 1st onwards, and not retroactively taxing income earned before January 1st. This is made even clearer by referring to the provisions of Article 26, Section 1 of the Detailed Implementation Rules. For Category 1, Items A and B, the business profits earned from January 1, 1937, onwards, if the settlement period is at the end of June, according to the provisions of Section 1 of that article, should be paid in one lump sum from August 1st to the end of October. This means that starting taxation from January 1st refers to clearly delineating the before and after boundaries of business profits, and does not mean that from January 1st, the business profits of 1936 must be retroactively paid together. The difference in this matter is significant. Based on the information in the letter, it is appropriate to prepare an official document to submit to your ministry for review and approval, and to provide clarification for compliance, which is beneficial to the public.

British Credit Loan to China: Total Amount is £10 Million, Stable Foreign Exchange After the Loan is Successful 131

Regarding the British credit loan to China, the New Voice News Agency reporter learned from banking circles yesterday morning that the total amount of the credit loan is said to be £10 million. This is the result of negotiations between Mr. Leith-Ross, the special envoy dispatched by Britain to China to investigate the economic situation, and the Chinese financial authorities. Although Mr. Leith-Ross has returned home, his assistants who came to China, Mr. Hall Patch (currently the financial advisor to the British Embassy in China) and Mr. Rogers (currently an advisor to the Chinese Ministry of Finance), are both in Shanghai. This credit loan is not cash; it involves British goods. The British trade in goods with China will inevitably be more prosperous than before. When Mr. Leith-Ross was in China, the total amount discussed was £20 million, but now it has been reduced by half to £10 million. After the credit loan is successful, China's foreign exchange can be further stabilized, which will benefit both China and Britain and will not have much impact on China's banking sector.

Jiangxi's Loan from the Bank of Communications and Four Other Banks Ceased 139

According to the New Voice News Agency, the Jiangxi Provincial Government's Industrial and Commercial Management Committee's plan to borrow 6 million yuan from the Bank of Communications, the Farmers Bank of China, the Jiangxi Yumin Bank, and four other banks to build agricultural warehouses and handle storage and pawn loans has now ceased because Xiao Chunjin, the director of the committee, has resigned, and the newly appointed Director of the Finance Department, Wen Qun, has set a new plan for agricultural relief. Therefore, the loan of 6 million yuan from the four banks has been terminated. As for the new plan, it stipulates that agricultural warehouses will be managed by the Jiangxi Rural Cooperative Committee, and the committee will set up cooperative credit unions in various counties to handle loans. The agricultural warehouses already operated by the Jiangxi Yumin Bank will be taken over by the committee. Any bank wishing to lend to agriculture in Jiangxi Province must notify the committee in advance, and the committee will handle it centrally. The above measures have been approved by the provincial government meeting.
