Villagers' Appeal: Difficulty Paying for Encroached Land 147

Because Jia Fujin lacks the funds to pay, they request no violation of the land outline. After the Shanghai Land Bureau surveyed the Yangjing area of Pudong, villagers were initially encouraged to exchange certificates because any encroached land could be temporarily approved for use. However, after Director Cai completely overturned the regulations regarding certificate application requirements, any encroached land now requires increased taxes and payment, otherwise, new certificates will never be issued. Consequently, those with substantial properties and profitable businesses can comply, but impoverished farmers whose land has been passed down through generations have no choice but to sell their homes to cover the Land Bureau's fees, or they cannot enjoy the rights of a landowner. The current landowner, Jia Dangjin, lacks the means to pay for the encroached land and has petitioned for its removal. The original petition is recorded below: A petition to request the Shanghai Land Bureau be instructed to approve the removal of encroached land to alleviate the people's hardship. I, a resident of 86 Jiajiage Road, Yangjing, Pudong, Shanghai, wish to register my ancestral home with the Land Bureau's certificate exchange office in December of the 23rd year of the Republic [1934]. I request an exchange for a new certificate. However, the bureau's staff claimed that the blueprint had been taken by Zhou Shaowen and asked that Zhou be notified to bring his certificate to the bureau for verification before a new certificate could be issued. This was delayed until February of this year when the blueprint was finally verified. Later, I received Land Bureau document number 将字第二二一, a notice stating, "... it is necessary to pay 125 yuan for the encroached land." However, due to rural bankruptcy in recent years and the lack of available work, I am unable to pay. I have repeatedly requested that the land be removed. I subsequently received Land Bureau document number 乙字第二五一九, which stated, "Received the petition... For the sake of maintaining complete household plots, the removal will not be permitted, and the price should be paid according to regulations." Given the current economic downturn, the lack of earning capacity, and the absence of property to sell, I am forced to cut into my own flesh to heal the wound, willing to request the removal of the encroached land. The Shanghai Land Bureau has repeatedly changed directors, and with each change, the regulations are altered. Previously, Article 12 of the Certificate Application Requirements stipulated that the use of a few fen or li of encroached land would be temporarily approved. Now, Director Cai has completely overturned this. The Land Bureau is now ignoring everything and rejecting the petition, which not only contradicts the purpose of the survey but also violates Article 19 of the Land Outline issued by the Executive Yuan's Order No. 3517 for general implementation, which states, "All land without tax or land with more land than tax will not be investigated retroactively, and free tax increases will be permitted without collecting supplementary tax fees or handling fees," and Article 28, "Land without a contract that has been peacefully occupied for a long time and is certified by neighbors as meeting the requirements of civil law shall be handled according to regulations." Therefore, I respectfully submit this petition, earnestly requesting your approval and instructing the Shanghai Land Bureau to approve the removal of the encroached land to alleviate the people's hardship, which would be a great kindness. Presented to Executive Yuan President Jiang and Vice President Kong, by petitioner Jia Fujin.

Da Hua Opium Case: Rescue Efforts Spread Like Wildfire; Shipping Association Cables Haimen Authorities to Rescue the Innocent and Avoid Implication 150

The Ping An Shipping Company's Wintai liner, Da Hua, departed Shanghai for Taiwan. When the ship arrived in Haimen, military police searched the ship and found a large quantity of opium in passenger Jiang Xinglian's luggage inside the chief mate Chuan Runian's cabin. The passenger, the chief mate, and the opium were taken to the Joint Investigation Office and transferred to the Fourth District Anti-Opium Brigade for interrogation. Brigade Commander Su interrogated Jiang Xinglian, who admitted to smuggling opium. Chief Mate Chuan Runian was interrogated and found to have no involvement in the case. Jiang Xinglian was punished according to the law, and Chuan Runian was found innocent and released back to the ship. This occurred on the 5th of this month. On the 6th, military police returned to the Da Hua and rearrested Chief Mate Chuan Runian. Because the opium was found in the chief mate's cabin, not in the passenger's cabin, suspicion arose. He was detained until the ship sailed and has not yet been released. The Da Hua returned to Shanghai yesterday, and the shipowner reported the incident to the company, requesting assistance in rescuing the chief mate. Simultaneously, a petition was submitted to the Shipping Industry Association requesting assistance. Chuan Runian has served Da Hua with loyalty and honesty and has never committed any offenses. The Shipping Industry Association has also conducted an investigation and confirmed that Chuan Runian was unaware of the opium smuggling and had no involvement. Therefore, Mr. Chu Qiaqing drafted a telegram to the Haimen authorities, proving that Chief Mate Chuan was not involved in the case, requesting his prompt release and avoiding implicating the innocent.

Using an Overweight Peck (Dou) That Exceeds the Standard Makes One Liable to Prosecution by the Authorities 153

The Dagong News Agency reports that the Changshu Guild in the city is using overweight pecks, causing endless harm to the rice transport merchants. A special petition was submitted to the Shanghai Social Bureau's Metrology Verification Institute and a letter was sent to the Bean and Rice Trade Association requesting prohibition to protect the interests of the shipping merchants. The institute replied to the Bean and Rice Trade Association yesterday, stating: "In response to your letter stating that the use of overweight pecks by the peck officers is causing endless harm and requesting a notice to prohibit and correct this, we have approved this. Overweight and underweight pecks are both illegal. The Municipal Social Bureau has fairly stipulated the standards, and public pecks with missing half-pecks are available at both the North and South City offices. If a dispute arises over overweight or underweight pecks, it can be reported to the office, and the rice will be fairly measured with the public peck. If it exceeds the standard, the authorities will be immediately petitioned to punish them severely according to the law. As for the so-called 'retaining a sample,' it has always been disallowed. Now, as before, we will issue a notice to the North and South City industries to consistently follow the established cases. We should hereby respond and hope you will note this for our information."

Lower Reaches of the Yangtze River: River Water Plummets by More Than Ten Feet; Jianghai Customs Received Reports of River Water Levels Along the River Yesterday; Hankou Gauge Insufficient at Twenty Feet 158

River Water Plummets by More Than Ten Feet

According to reports received yesterday by Jianghai Customs from various customs ports in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, the river water level has plummeted by more than ten feet. Our correspondent from Datong News Agency has recorded the situation as follows: The water level in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River has been quite stable recently. After the Hankou water level retreated to within thirty feet, the water level on the first day of this month was twenty-eight feet one inch. Jiujiang on the same day was thirty feet zero one inch, Anqing on the same day was twenty-eight feet, and Wuhu on the same day was nineteen feet four inches. Unexpectedly, according to reports from various ports downstream received by Jianghai Customs yesterday, the water levels have all plummeted by more than ten feet. The Hankou water level yesterday retreated to seventeen feet five inches, Jiujiang yesterday retreated to nineteen feet six inches, and Wuhu yesterday retreated to twelve feet nine inches.

Stopping the Lighting of Flood Water Buoys

Because of the sharp drop in the Yangtze River's water level, the flood water buoys and temporary lightships set up by the customs to guide ships during the flood season are no longer necessary. Yesterday, the Anqing waterway flood water buoys, the Huangshiji flood water temporary lightship, and the Huanglian Old flood water buoys were removed. The customs has also issued shipping notices, ordering Shanghai-Hankou shipping lines to pay attention.

After Ge Guanfu, a worker in the letterpress department of this newspaper, was tragically murdered on the 13th of this month, the details have been recorded in this newspaper. A grand funeral was held at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, and many colleagues from this newspaper went to offer condolences. However, it was found that Mr. Ge's family was in dire straits, leaving behind an elderly mother, a younger sister, and a young daughter. The text of the petition is recorded as follows: "For the murder of a husband, the murderer is at large, we earnestly request that you uphold humanity, immediately forward this petition to the Municipal Police Bureau, and swiftly arrest the murderer to uphold human life. Ge Guanfu, a worker of this newspaper, at about 3:00 p.m. on the 13th of this month, at his residence at No. 11 Sandu Lane, Daji Road, Nanshi, was murdered by his adulterous wife Liu Xiangbao and her lover, Mr. Lin, who conspired to chop his neck with a kitchen knife, killing him on the spot. The murderers took the opportunity to escape. The detailed situation has been recorded in various newspapers in this city, which your union is surely aware of and need not be elaborated upon. However, it has been found that the location of the case is within the jurisdiction of the Ximen Branch of the Nanshi Public Security Bureau. If the adulterer and adulteress are allowed to remain at large, not only will the deceased suffer injustice in the afterlife, but all the members of the union, as colleagues, who witnessed the tragic scene, will also feel ashamed towards the deceased friend. Therefore, we have no choice but to submit this petition to your union, to immediately forward it to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, to instruct its subordinates, and to issue a document to the police authorities of the special district to quickly arrest the murderer, to bring the adulterer and adulteress to justice as soon as possible, to punish them according to the law, to uphold human life, and to maintain law and order. We await your orders with respect. Submitted to the Shanghai Newspaper Workers' Union." Furthermore, it is reported that after the Ge Guanfu case occurred, his relatives went to the Public Security Bureau to report that before Ge Guanfu died, Liu had instructed her cousin Guo Jufu (over twenty years old, from Changzhou, residing at No. 9 Fude Lane, Wuzhen Road, Zhabei) to bring four conditions: (1) No abuse allowed, (2) Mother-in-law and husband's sisters not allowed to visit (Ge has three sisters, two married, and one sister who is only thirteen years old), (3) Move to another place of residence, (4) Pay a certain amount of living expenses each month. Ge believed that he could not neglect his mother or abandon his sisters, and that the conditions were harsh, so he did not agree. These conditions are still with Guo, who intends to negotiate further. Guo Jufu's mother received six hundred yuan in rent in her village when Guo was eleven years old. At that time, Guo and his father were both in Shanghai, and Liu was not yet married. She sent a letter to Shanghai, saying that Guo's mother had died suddenly. Guo rushed back to his wife's home for the funeral. When he held his mother's head while placing her in the coffin, blood gushed out from her neck, which had also been severed. Ge Guanfu's death was a replica of this. After investigation by the detective team, it was determined that Guo Jufu's past and the circumstances of his mother's unjust death, Liu's participation in Guo's mother's funeral before she was married, and her husband's current tragic death, made it necessary to investigate Guo Jufu. Therefore, Guo was arrested and interrogated the day before yesterday.

Firecracker Industry Increases Prices Yesterday: Due to Rising Prices in Production Areas, Increased Transportation Costs 162

The Shanghai Firecracker Industry Association, due to rising prices in production areas and increased transportation costs, has implemented a price increase starting yesterday to maintain its capital. Tongde Hospital: Tuberculosis Prevention X-ray Examination 163

More than 20% of those examined within a month are patients. Tongde Hospital on Tongfu Road in this city, in order to promote tuberculosis prevention work, has specially organized lung X-ray examinations. For the sake of popularization, each person is charged only a handling fee of one yuan, middle school students are charged only eight cents, and elementary school students are charged six cents. Since its inception, many people from all walks of life have come to be examined. According to reports from Dr. Gu Yuqi and Dr. Gu Zuren of the hospital, a total of 428 people were examined in September, and more than 20% of them had lung diseases. A total of 96 students were examined, and more than 19% of them had lung diseases. This phenomenon among a small number of students is truly alarming. It also shows the large number of people suffering from lung diseases, and those concerned about tuberculosis prevention work should pay close attention and find ways to cooperate in prevention. It is reported that the hospital has submitted the examination results to the Social Bureau and the Health Bureau for statistics and has decided to continue to give preferential treatment to all sectors of society to promote popularization.

The manager of the Central Huili Ball Field on Avenue Albert in the French Concession, the Spaniard Yasuosen (transliteration), previously received extortion letters from bandits demanding 500,000 yuan, stating that those who were willing to negotiate in good faith could contact Huang Yuanliang at the Dongya Hotel. He immediately reported this to the French police, who prepared a letter of consent to negotiate and placed it in the Dongya Hotel. Detectives, led by Zhou Buguang, waited. On the 30th of last month, Yang Yiping went to retrieve the letter and was immediately arrested, brought back, and sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention. During the investigation, it was also discovered that Yang had written a letter to Mayor Wu Tiecheng of this city in the name of Song Yuanyuan, who resided at No. 89 Feifangfang, requesting relief. Wu sent his secretary, surnamed Guo, to meet with him, invited Yang to a meal, and gave him one yuan for pocket money. He also wrote a letter in the name of Ye Zujin to Deputy Director Yuan Chongzhi of the Nanjing Supervisory Yuan, requesting assistance. The French Police Department believed that the case was complex and that the investigation would take time, so it requested the Second Special Court to postpone the trial. The investigation by the French Police Department has been completed. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the Second Special Court presided over the interrogation in the Second Criminal Court. Yuan Jiahua, the lawyer representing the French Police Department, stated that the defendant wrote extortion letters, demanding 500,000 yuan from the plaintiff. The words in the letter were all detrimental to the plaintiff. In addition, it was discovered that the defendant forged a seal in the name of Song Yuanyuan, wrote a letter to Mayor Wu, and defrauded him of money. He is now being prosecuted under Articles 346 and 217 of the Criminal Law for extortion by intimidation and forgery of seals. The defendant Yang Yiping stated that he had never been to the Huili Ball Field and knew nothing about the extortion letters. He came to Shanghai to escape marriage and was living in the Dongya Hotel, owing rent that he could not pay. Because he was starving, he wrote letters to Mayor Wu and Deputy Director Xu, requesting help. Last month, he saw a letter from Huang Yuanliang at the Dongya Hotel and remembered that he had a classmate named Huang Yuanliang in the Philippines, so he took the letter and was arrested. At this point, the court noted that the police report was lengthy and that there was no time to review it in detail, so the hearing was adjourned to the morning of the 23rd. The defendant was returned to custody.

French Police Crack Down on Cricket Gambling Den: Ye Mingji Sentenced to One Month Imprisonment; Assistants and Gamblers Fined 168

The French Police, led by West Detective Biel (transliteration) and Chinese Detective Liu Kunbao, learned a few days ago that a rogue named Zhang Laosan was recently running a private cricket gambling den at No. 80, Lane 125, Caishi Road. Every night, many people were lured into the den to gamble, and the wins and losses were quite large. The owner collected 15 cents for every yuan bet, making a substantial profit. There was a strict ban on gambling, so at noon that day, the police, along with detectives Chen Tinghuai, Yuan Zhonghe, and Chen Zhiban, rushed to the address and searched the premises. The gambling boss, Zhang Laosan, had already fled upon hearing the news. Only the bookkeeper Ye Mingji, the assistants Gu Peigen, Su Pingan, Cai Heshang, Ma Huaide, Zhao Renbao, Zhang Gongjian, Mu Xiaoshan, Qin Liansheng, and thirty-three gamblers, including Huang Shen and Lu Chunting (who work at the China Merchants Automobile Company), Yu Xingen, and others, were apprehended. Twenty-four cricket jars, basins, and fighting cages, as well as more than forty yuan in gambling money in the form of large and small banknotes and copper coins, were seized and taken to the police station. Yesterday, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Branch Court for trial. Judge Qiu presided over the trial, and Gu Shouxi, a lawyer from the Police Department, presented the case and prosecuted under Article 268 of the Criminal Law. During the court's questioning of the defendants, most of them tried to evade and deny the charges. The judge ruled that the evidence was complete and that there was no room for denial. He immediately sentenced Ye Mingji to one month's imprisonment, the assistants Gu Peigen and others to a fine of eight yuan each, and the gamblers to a fine of four yuan each as a warning. All confiscated items were confiscated as per the list.

Qin Cainan's Residential Mortgage Dispute 169

Qin Cainan, a 51-year-old Wuxi native involved in the international drug trafficking case, was arrested by the French police for the drug case and sent to the Second Special Court for public prosecution. As a result, he was sentenced to two years' imprisonment and a fine of 4,000 yuan. Qin refused to accept the verdict and repeatedly appealed to the High Third Branch Court and the Supreme Court, which remanded the case for retrial. The original sentence of imprisonment and fine was upheld. He is currently appealing to the Supreme Court. During the appeal period, he paid 15,000 yuan in cash as bail. In October 1934, due to litigation, Qin mortgaged his residence at No. 725 Foch Road, French Registration No. 953, land and buildings, to the Siming Savings Association on Nanjing Road for 80,000 yuan, with a one-year redemption period. When the term expired, Qin was unable to redeem the property. On August 15th of this year, the auctioneer, Xie, according to Article 878 of the Civil Code, after negotiating with the debtor, sold the entire mortgaged property at a price of 96,786.50 yuan to the creditor and entered into a contract. Currently, Qin resides in the house and refuses to move out. Therefore, the Siming Savings Association has appointed a lawyer to file a lawsuit with the Civil Court of the Second Special Court against Qin Cainan for the delivery of the property, as well as interest calculated at ten yuan per day from August 16th of this year until the date of execution, and to bear the litigation costs. The court, based on the complaint, summoned the parties to the Seventh Civil Court yesterday, presided over by Judge Ma Yishu. Both parties were represented by lawyers. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated the facts and reasons for the lawsuit, requesting a judgment on the object of the suit. The defendant's representative, lawyer Sun Zuji, responded by requesting the dismissal of the plaintiff's claim and the request for provisional execution, stating that the defendant's agreement with the plaintiff was entered into out of necessity. At the time of the agreement, both parties agreed to postpone the disposal of the property for six months from the date of the agreement because the defendant's property was worth more than the estimated value. The defendant is currently residing in the property and is seeking a buyer to sell it at a good price in order to repay the plaintiff's debt. There were letters exchanged between the parties after the agreement, which are presented as evidence. The plaintiff's lawyer further stated that although there was a six-month postponement of the disposal, it was not a promise that the defendant could reside in the property but rather a promise that the defendant could find a new buyer within six months. After further arguments by both lawyers, the court announced the conclusion of the debate and scheduled the judgment for 9:00 a.m. on the 20th.

Forged Traffic Banknotes Discovered on the Market: The Names of the Eastern Three Provinces Traffic Banknotes Were Cut Off, and the Names of the Shanghai Banknotes Were Pasted on Seamlessly; The Original Banknotes Were Slightly Burned and Could Still Be Exchanged for New Banknotes 170

Recently, a type of counterfeit legal tender from the Traffic Bank that had been patched up was discovered on the market. Because the patching technique was quite ingenious, it was difficult to detect the fraud. These patched banknotes were originally issued by banks in the Eastern Three Provinces. Because the banknotes issued by banks in that area were no longer in circulation after the Incident of the Three Eastern Provinces, some criminals took the opportunity to collect these banknotes, cut off the most important parts of the banknotes, such as the drawing in the middle and the name of the issuing bank, and replaced them with the drawing and the name of the Shanghai Traffic Bank. In this way, the useless banknotes from outside the customs became Traffic Bank legal tender. The cut banknotes were then slightly burned around the edges to expose the burnt marks, and then used to exchange for new banknotes at the Traffic Bank as "fire-damaged" banknotes. In short, after this procedure, one Traffic Bank banknote could be used as two, and the worthless banknotes from outside the customs could be used again. Compared to counterfeiting legal tender, this method was not only less costly and more profitable, but also simpler. As a result, patched banknotes appeared frequently on the market, and it was easy to be deceived if one was not careful. The Traffic Bank had also received these counterfeit banknotes and was now paying close attention to them and trying to eradicate them, as they were a menace to the financial community. The day before yesterday afternoon at 5:00 p.m., Chuan Yi, a 36-year-old Cantonese man, together with Yang Yizhong, an apprentice from a money shop at No. 461 Sichuan Road, went to the Traffic Bank and took out eighteen Traffic Bank banknotes, each worth one yuan, with the drawing and the name of the bank in the middle cut off, leaving burnt marks and the numbers on the left and right completely intact, and requested to exchange them for new banknotes. The bank staff carefully inspected each banknote and saw that the damage was similar on each, and that it was not due to fire damage. Suspecting that they were patched banknotes, they instructed the bank's investigator, Hong Yutian, to take Chuan, Yang, and the original banknotes to the general police station. After questioning, it was confirmed that Yang was not involved and was released. Detectives Kang Zengxiang and Sun Jishan escorted Chuan to his residence at No. 16 Yongdeli, Tianjin Road, and searched the premises, finding one ten-yuan banknote that had been completely patched up, and several five-yuan, ten-yuan, fifty-yuan, and one-hundred-yuan banknotes with the name of the Guangdong Provincial Bank printed on them, totaling 12,700 yuan, and took them back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, Chuan, along with witnesses Yang Yizhong and Hong Yutian, escorted Chuan and the counterfeit banknotes to the First Special District Local Court. Judge Feng Shide conducted the interrogation. The police lawyer, Ru Bao Yi, stated the circumstances of the case. Because the case was important and required a detailed investigation, it was requested that the suspect be temporarily detained for investigation. The court then questioned Chuan Yi and ordered him to be detained for further interrogation in seven days.

Woman's Hospital Body Burial Case: Zhang Yao Has No Connection; Court Revokes Arrest Warrant 171

Zhang Wenhua, a doctor at the Hongkou Women's Hospital at No. 290 Zhaofeng Road, and his concubine Chen Xiaobao were arrested and sent to the First Special Court on September 4 of this year for conspiring to kill a woman named Lu Aili and a man named Yu Gengsheng who had abortions, and burying their bodies underground. The interrogation has been completed and the verdict is scheduled to be announced on the 20th of this month. However, the police have been strictly investigating Zhang Wenhua's wife, Zhang Yao (39 years old, from Shanghai), and have been unable to arrest her in Pudong, so they requested that the Special Court issue an arrest warrant. The police finally arrested Zhang Yao. However, because she was six months pregnant and about to give birth, she was sent to the Ximen Women and Children's Hospital. She gave birth to a daughter a few days ago. The Chinese and Western detectives of the police station have been conducting a detailed investigation into Zhang Yao's criminal involvement for days. The result of the investigation determined that Zhang Yao had no connection to the murder and body burning case. Therefore, Judge Zhong Qing of the First Court presided over the hearing in the Third Criminal Court yesterday morning. When the police handed over the case, the police lawyer, Zhang Shizhu, immediately stated the previous situation and requested that the arrest warrant be revoked. Judge Zhong ruled that Zhang Yao's arrest warrant should be revoked.

Assassination of a Man on Jiaozhou Road; Police Solve the Case; Victim Shot in Fourteen Places; Gatekeeper Zhang Huaisheng Arrested 172

On the night of the 11th of this month, at approximately 10 p.m., an assassination occurred near Lane 273 of Jiaozhou Road near Yanping Road in West Shanghai. The Gordon Road police station, upon hearing the alarm, dispatched investigators to investigate. The assailant(s) had already fled. A man appearing to be 35 or 36 years old was found lying on his back in a pool of blood, covered in bullet wounds. The total number of wounds, large and small, amounted to fourteen. He was rushed by vehicle to the Red Cross Hospital, but died en route. The body was sent to the coroner's office for examination and

orders were given to arrest the perpetrator(s).

It is now known that after this case occurred, the responsible Gordon Road police station specially dispatched Chinese detective Liu Zhengang to conduct a detailed investigation for several days. He discovered that the deceased was named Kang Wenjin, from Anhui, residing at 940 Dongma Li, Binlang Road. Based on various clues, at approximately 6 a.m. the previous morning, Zhang Huaisheng, an Anhui native working as a gatekeeper, suspected of the crime, was arrested at 940 Dongma Li and taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Eighth Criminal Tribunal of the First Special District Court to request his detention. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, then presented the case, detailing the

Investigation Process,

stating that on the night of the 11th of this month, at around 10 p.m., Chinese police officer No. 2920 from the Gordon Road police station was patrolling near the scene when suddenly several gunshots were heard at the intersection of Yanping Road and Jiaozhou Road. He rushed to investigate and found a man lying in a pool of blood in Lane 273, with numerous gunshot wounds. He immediately reported to the police station by telephone and ordered an ambulance to take the injured person to the Red Cross Hospital. However, he died en route before treatment could be administered. The body was sent to the coroner's office. An investigation was launched, but because the area was remote, with few people around, and the deceased's clothing was tattered, it was assumed that he was from the criminal underworld, so it was decided that the motive was not robbery for profit but

a premeditated revenge killing.

Further investigation revealed that the deceased had fourteen bullet wounds of varying sizes on his front and back. Based on this, it was determined that there were at least two assailants at the time, each wielding a handgun, who had engaged in a fierce struggle with the deceased, resulting in his clothes being torn. In addition to several shell casings recovered at the scene, three pieces of paper were found on the deceased: one was a registration form, one was a remittance receipt, and the other was a pawn ticket from the Renhe pawnshop. The police contacted the post office and were informed that a Mr. Kang from 400 Binlang Road had

come to send money.

Chinese and foreign detectives immediately went to Binlang Road to investigate, but there was no number 400. Therefore, the address written on the postal form was forged. They then went to Renhe Pawnshop and found that on September 28, a Mr. Kang from 940 Tongmao Li, Binlang Road, had pawned a small leather suitcase for two yuan, one jiao, and five fen. Because the original pawn ticket had been lost, a guarantor was required to issue a replacement, as per the regulations. Therefore, Xu Yongxing Tobacco and Paper Shop at 131 Tongmao Li provided a seal of guarantee. The police retrieved the pawned suitcase and, upon inspection, found

several slips of paper inside.

These were the contact information for a certain police detective captain and a draft by a certain Yin, discussing a dispute over women. They then went to Xu Yongxing Tobacco and Paper Shop to investigate. The shop owners, Xu Jinshan and his wife, Xu, stated that they did not know Kang Wenjin and that Zhang Huaisheng, who worked as a gatekeeper, had introduced them to act as guarantors. Zhang lived at 940 Tongmao Li, and so on. Chinese and foreign detectives secretly investigated the area and found many men and women entering and exiting 940, all of whom were from Anhui. Therefore, yesterday morning, they

detained the men and women

fifteen people in the room. After Mrs. Xu identified one of them as Zhang Huaisheng, Zhang was arrested and the others were released. It was confirmed that Zhang had previously been employed as a gatekeeper by the Hardoon Company, but was dismissed on the 7th of this month after being accused of extortion. The police stated that the investigation procedures were not yet complete, and that the handgun used to kill Kang Wenjin was found to be the same one used in the

robbery and injury

at the Lafayette Theatre on Lafayette Road on April 19 of this year, and in the attempted robbery and shooting at 121 Lime Kiln, Caojiadu. Therefore, they requested permission to detain him. They then presented all the evidence. Zhang Huaisheng denied the accusations, stating that he did not know the deceased or the owner of Xu Yongxing Tobacco and Paper Shop. Judge Huang Risheng reviewed the confession and ordered Zhang to be detained for seven days for further review.

Minimum Freight; All Subject to Surcharge 176

The Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau issued a business circular from the Ministry of Railways, stating that: Upon investigation, the minimum freight charges collected by various railways, those that should be subject to surcharges are collected separately from the minimum freight of 5 jiao. The surcharge percentages vary from railway to railway, resulting in inconsistent total minimum fees. Railway merchants find this inconvenient. Furthermore, goods with surcharges calculated by volume or item as stipulated in the tariff table have been exempt from surcharges. Minimum freight should also be exempt to standardize and facilitate calculation. It is now specially stipulated that regardless of whether the goods are in full carloads or less than full carloads, the minimum freight will be exempt from surcharges, effective November 1 of this year. Clause 2 of the instructions No. 3684, Lianzi, issued by this Ministry on October 16 of last year, regarding the calculation of surcharges, should not apply to minimum freight. Furthermore, the ferry fee for crossing the river in the capital should still be collected separately and is not included in the minimum freight. In addition to separate orders, you are hereby instructed to comply and implement accordingly. The Bureau has instructed the Transportation Department to handle this matter.

After entrusting accountant Xu Yongzuo as the liquidator, the liquidator issued a public announcement yesterday: After Tongyi Bank ceased operations last year, this accountant was entrusted to investigate the accounts, collect outstanding debts, and settle liabilities. Shareholders' meetings were convened twice to discuss measures for advancement, but resolutions could not be reached because the number of shareholders present did not meet the statutory quorum. Currently, 70-80% of the external liabilities have been settled. At the resumed special shareholders' meeting on the 12th of this month, the shareholders present met the statutory quorum. They all agreed that the situation of the times and the market was worse than at the time of the suspension of operations, and there was no hope of resumption. Therefore, a public resolution was made to dissolve and liquidate, in order to bring matters to a close. This accountant was selected as the liquidator. In addition to accepting the appointment and reporting for record, all creditors of the bank are requested to bring their creditor certificates to this office for registration before the end of this month, for verification purposes. All debtors are also requested to send the full amount of their outstanding debts to this office for verification and receipt within the aforementioned period, in order to clear their liabilities. Please do not delay. This is a special announcement.

Chief Clerk of Shanghai District Court; Xuan Maohe Passes Away 179

Xuan Maohe, Chief Clerk of the Shanghai District Court, was from Zhuji, Shaoxing, and was 31 years old. He was a promising young man. He was originally a prospective judge of the Wuxian District Court and was highly valued by President Lu Yimei. When President Lu was transferred to the Shanghai Court, he specially transferred Xuan to fill this position, using the authority of the chief clerk to provide assistance. Since taking office, he has been extremely thorough in reforming court affairs and reorganizing lower-level staff. President Lu and Chief Prosecutor Zhu relied on him greatly. Just as they were planning to make use of his talents, Xuan recently contracted a distended abdomen and hemoptysis, with swelling all over his body, rendering him unable to move. He sought treatment at the Nanyang Hospital, but unfortunately, his illness was beyond cure, and medical treatment was ineffective. He passed away the night before last. President Lu and Chief Prosecutor Zhu were extremely saddened upon hearing the news and personally took care of the funeral arrangements. Yesterday, the coffin was moved to the Yongxi Hall of the Shaoxing Guild Hall, pending the arrival of his elder brother in Shanghai for the funeral. The vacant position has been temporarily filled by Jin Lu, the Chief Clerk of the Records Section, by appointment of the President. Mr. Jin has served in the District Court for twenty years and is a capable man.

Letter 187

To the Editor,

On the 13th of this month, I read a news item in your newspaper titled "Yichang Enamelware Store Robbed," which was slightly inconsistent with the facts. I hope you will grant a correction to clarify the truth and list the details of my capture of the robber as follows: At 9 p.m. on the 12th of this month, I was on the Route 6 French Concession tram in Laoximen and got off at Xiaqiao, planning to visit relatives in Hengqing Lane, Beile Road. Unexpectedly, when I reached the entrance of Huizhong Middle School, I suddenly heard a cry of "Catch the thief!" in front of me. I saw a person wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers running towards me, and the person chasing him kept shouting "Catch the thief!" At that time, I was moved by passion and, regardless of everything, bravely stepped forward to chase the thief. The thief then crossed the French Concession iron gate and fled towards the South Manufacturing Bureau Road. I followed him to the intersection of Manufacturing Bureau Road and Xie Xu Road, about nine feet away from the thief. I jumped up and tackled the thief to the ground, and I also fell on the thief's back. I tightly held the thief's hand, pulled him up, and held on to him. Later, the victim called for the police officer on duty, who arrived. I directed the police officer to hold the thief's upper body (near the arm), and then I seized the handgun. We then captured him. The report in your newspaper said that I and Wang Tongjie, police officer No. 19 of the Tangjiawan Police Station, gave chase, and the thief drew his gun to resist arrest, but the gun jammed and he was captured. It also said that a four-inch white Langlin handgun and six bullets were seized on the spot. This is inconsistent with the facts. The thief's handgun and bullets were all seized by me, and there is evidence to prove it (that is, after the thief was captured, I seized the handgun and immediately walked to the Ximen Sub-bureau to hand over the thief. During the transfer, I used the seized handgun as a protective weapon to guard against the thief's escape. When I arrived at the duty room of the Ximen Sub-bureau, I personally handed the gun over to a clerk named Huang for safekeeping. Upon inspection, it was discovered that the gun was loaded with bullets, so the clerk took it out for detailed inspection. The bullet had been struck by the firing pin, but fortunately the bullet failed to fire, otherwise I would have suffered an unexpected misfortune. However, it can be seen that the thief was ferocious. The above-mentioned situation was also explained in detail by the victim, Ou Fusheng, at the Ximen Sub-bureau. If the handgun had been obtained by the police officer on duty, why was I holding it in my hand all the way to escort the thief? Why did I personally hand over the gun and bullets to the bureau? There is no reason for me to have seized a four-inch white Langlin handgun and bullets on the spot with the police officer on duty. Therefore, I am writing to inform your newspaper of the detailed circumstances, hoping that you will grant a correction to dispel public doubts. This is addressed to the Great Editor of the Shen Bao Newspaper. Respectfully submitted by Mo Ruo Min, October 14.

In Turmoil 188

— Fei Er

In turmoil, the crowd and vehicles flow on the street. From north to south, these few days have been suddenly tense, suddenly lonely, and then suddenly lively again. Like a festering sore, that unbearable pus bursts out of the suppression and then flows onto the street: first the beautiful cars, heavy carts, then rickshaws, "tiger" carts (two-wheeled carts), and even vehicles on two feet; first the beautiful suits, long gowns, and qipaos for autumn, then short jackets and shorts, and among these adults are ignorant children, and even some carrying infants in their arms.

The air is like lead, and what cannot be spread is the depression in people's hearts; it is also like flying poplar catkins, scattered everywhere in the wind and rain. Rumors have taken flight, flying everywhere; with the facts before them, the enemy's weapons shake the courage of the bereaved.

Does anyone know where there is a safe home now; home is under other people's eaves. Frightened souls cannot withstand the devastation of much wind and rain, where is the soul of the nation?

Poor, helpless, weak people, where are you going?

Walking through the crowded streets, watching the tides of people flow. On the sidewalks, and even at the intersecting street corners, what are groups of rolling eyes looking at? Cars, non-stop cars; people, endless people. On the roads in the countryside, people will suspect that a disaster has occurred in the countryside, that floods have occurred somewhere, or that the sun has dried up the entire village? The refugees, in the cities, form rows, without flags, without new or old music, just rows of cars, rows of people: all the means of transportation of several centuries, from cars to a single carrying pole; all the clothing of several centuries, from the new style of 1937 to mud-covered trousers.

What else is there to say? You see there is a chamber pot, a straw mat, or a tattered suitcase... Chairs, screens, all kinds of furniture are complete. And the people? An old woman is holding her little grandson, and a villager is sitting on a "tiger" cart. Workers and farmers are walking on foot. It is happiness to have a car to sit in.

"Mom, I want to sit in that car." A child is crying.

The woman's brow is furrowed.

"What car?"

The child's finger points to a beautiful car that suddenly slides past them with a growl.

The policeman's hand grabs a cushion.

The rickshaw puller pleads:

"Thank you!"...

A stick comes down.

"Get out of here, get out of here. Run, run. Go to the countryside to escape!"

"Tch!" A voice laughs from the crowd.

"Hit them! Let them hit them! They should be hit!" The voice of the entire city and village.

Listen! How mixed the sound of the city is!

"Whoosh..."

"Squeak..."

"Tuk-tuk..."

Sunset and Falling Leaves 189

Twilight Musings 190

— Chuyang

Lately, every time evening approaches, a sense of vague agitation arises within me, much like the autumn willows in the private garden outside the window, swaying in the evening breeze.

——Is it autumn melancholy? The sorrow of a fallen nation? Or the troubles of life, the weariness brought on by illness?

I myself am at a loss for an answer, only feeling uneasy staying inside, flipping through a newspaper aimlessly. A copy of "Pastoral Symphony" that I was just reading on the desk is blown shut by the wind, and I think of Gide's line: "How happy those without eyes must be!" My heart sinks even further...

This small attic room is so cramped that apart from a bed, a table, and a chair, there's no room to move. If I want to rest, the only option is to lie down on the bed. On the bed is a letter I received this afternoon. A friend studying at a university in Jiangwan wrote at the end of his letter: "The unsettling situation from this time last year has reappeared before my eyes. People are moving away in an endless stream, and we are startled multiple times a night, making it hard to feel at peace. I can't help but envy the tranquility you and others enjoy."

——Ah, who can still be at peace?

Anyone with Chinese blood cannot be at peace!

Not being able to be at peace doesn't mean one can simply sulk in an attic room. Intellectuals are forever neurotic sentimentalists, their bodies and minds in a state of weak contradiction. ——Again, I scold myself like this.

I jump up and look at the sky. It's not devoid of clouds, and the setting sun is casting a few golden rays, mixed with a layer of smog. The sky in this city is always more depressing than bright. A loud thud from below startles me. It turns out it's the young couple living downstairs pushing their beautiful baby carriage out for a walk. Watching their slender and petite figures slowly walk towards the entrance of the alley, I can't help but feel my own loneliness. I originally wanted to go for a walk too, but the thought of aimlessly wandering around alone in the cool air is unappealing, so I hesitate again. The illusion of a home floats into my mind: Could it be that I am also longing for a partner, a home?

Home prospers the nation, women and life... life is spent amidst the troubles of these desires and wills. I hope there will be a bright tomorrow, but today's twilight feels like an endless twilight!

China Through the Eyes of a "Sinologist" 191

— Yu

After cutting open the belly to inspect, there isn't a drop of ink inside, yet those who demand a stomach full of well-reasoned strategies are still us, the literary hacks who piece together words like Tangrams. The donkey turns the millstone, turning and turning, still getting nowhere. But the donkey is forgivable. Its turning of the millstone is not voluntary but forced. On the donkey, we can see the yoke on its shoulders, the "blinders" over its eyes. Behind it, we can also hear the driver's shouts of "Giddy up!" or the whip's threatening "crack." The donkey is pitiful, we can't help but think. But when it is unharnessed, given some fodder, or the master shows favor by adding some extra beans and wheat, or gently pats its back, the donkey feels infinitely honored, and it "bellows" a few times, pleased with itself. To the master, this is a tactic, but to the donkey, it merely reveals its clumsy pitiableness.

The donkey turning the millstone is an age-old matter; however, to lead out the donkey and make a show of force is as ridiculous as leading a dog to plow the field. Therefore, when a pack of wolves comes before us, instead of drawing bows and setting arrows, we use the donkey, just unharnessed from the millstone, to "bellow loudly" in an attempt to scare them away. This is simply a trick as clumsy as the donkey itself.

Although there may be donkeys that can act "foolishly clever" and put on tiger skin, the piercing of the tiger skin is only a matter of time. Of course, as far as the donkey is concerned, it sees itself as a behemoth, but "his skill stops there," as someone has already said. But besides this skill, what else is there to do?

The donkey itself imagines that it is full of abilities, just as we imagine that we have a thousand hands and feet, and we imagine that we have many glorious titles. But someone has already told me that the "crown" that was never crowned has been placed in the corner of the toilet, and the hat we wear on our heads is made of paper, similar to the pointed paper hat that people put on us when we are paraded through the streets for public indignation. If we know this, the best way is not to be nosy, just as donkeys don't have to be nosy and bellow. So, in extraordinary times, we who are completely useless, even if we are useful, can at most help the scene and join the fun. That's all. Otherwise, even if there is a brilliant opinion, it can be told to the heart. Going to draft a ten-thousand-word policy proposal, one must feel that where does one begin? It's impossible, and yet stubbornly wants to say it, and there is a way. That is to copy "clichés." But if you copy the Chinese, you have to guard against people giving you the title of "plagiarist." The best way, then, is to copy foreigners.

Here I am copying foreigners' articles. (Because the technology is not advanced, I can't even copy completely, I naturally can't manage much.)

I once read Ms. Pearl Buck's great essay, "China Against Japan," in this year's American magazine Asia, who is known as a Chinese expert. After reading such a mysterious judgment, I felt unhappy, first because she extremely praised Japan. Here I have to declare that my unhappiness is not because she praises Japan. If I am unhappy because of praising Japan, some people may say that I have been poisoned by narrow nationalism. But I believe I am not a blind nationalist. The reason why I oppose her argument is because, like other imperialist scholars, she regards imperialist aggression as a mission for an excellent nation to civilize a backward nation. She believes that Japan's seizure of China is materially beneficial to China, roads will be built, commerce will be developed, disasters will be prevented, politics will be put on track, bandits will disappear, factories will be added, and the railway network will run through the entire country. It is so in material terms, and in terms of spiritual construction, illiteracy will decrease day by day, and the hygiene situation will be greatly improved. China's trachoma, lung disease, malaria, and hookworms will be greatly reduced. "No one can deny these facts." I really suspect that such words came from the mouth of the "Wangdao Paradise" propagator, and I don't believe that they came from the mouth of an American woman who had a relationship with China but had nothing to do with Japan. I don't know what she is based on to do the duty of propaganda for imperialism. This is one point that I oppose in her brilliant opinion.

The second point is that she is a believer in weapons alone. She says that China cannot resist Japan in the war because China has no equipment to speak of except for a large number of untrained people who can be used as cannon fodder. It really treats Chinese people as worse than the Indian tribes in her noble country. We know that since the founding of the United States, although those Indians have been "tamed" and their land has been gradually plundered. And drive them to the so-called reserved area. Such work took centuries to complete. Until the middle of the nineteenth century, Indian resistance was still heard from time to time. In the middle, the US government had suffered several defeats. I don't believe that a great nation of 400 million people can be easily used as cannon fodder, as she said. The origin of this impression may be because the Chinese themselves are too dragging in some places. The three northeastern provinces and Rehe were occupied without resistance, and the troops of Ji Province withdrew after being frightened by people. Those foreigners who call themselves Chinese experts but actually know nothing will naturally feel that the Chinese can only be used as cannon fodder and have no other use.

Third, what I object to is that she simply regards the Chinese as "precious goods" who cherish their lives and are selfish and self-interested. Naturally, it cannot be said that there are no such people among the Chinese, but she puts the stigma of humiliation on the head of the Chinese nation, but we dare not accept it. Although she did not have the malicious intentions of the neighboring Japanese officer Takashi Matsushita, who she admired, who said that the "vast majority of Chinese officials and people are mostly confused by profit and ignore the country, and even willingly harm the country. Their purpose is only to solve the desires of one's own official group, and they don't care about the country or the people's livelihood", she committed the same superficial mistake. She said, "On a personal level, the Chinese are adaptable, and if they don't have great enjoyment, even ordinary small pleasures are willing to accept. At the same time, failure is not a shame for them, and success is not a joy. They only give up dying when they cannot survive to the last limit, and regard life as more precious than honor, ambition, and patriotism.

Are all Chinese people as she said? I don't want to go to the long history of China to prove it with people, because those people already belong to the past. And the people who are alive and live among us, I can find many classes and types of people to prove that not all Chinese people can be classified into this category.

I always feel that those so-called "experts" are like many so-called experts in academics who only have a smattering of knowledge. They first establish a big premise, and simplify all the phenomena in the universe and include them in front of that big premise. They don't ask whether that big premise itself is accurate, and they also don't ask whether all phenomena can be included in that big premise to draw a conclusion. Their only goal is to grasp that big premise that they think they are right, and quickly find a conclusion. Being able to get a conclusion, regardless of whether the conclusion is true, their goal has been achieved, and they can ignore everything else. Therefore, those foreign "China Experts" only need to have been to Shanghai once, or ran a few miles from Shanghai, or read a few Chinese books, or met a few Chinese people, or saw a few Chinese things, and they think they already know China and the Chinese. So, after talking with these few Chinese people, or picking up a few things they have seen and heard, they say "that is China," or say "this is the Chinese." Furthermore, from these few things and these few people, they infer: "This is the fate of China." As a result, the Chinese in One Thousand and One Nights appear in front of foreigners, the Chinese cultural relics in the Ancient Palace Museum appear in front of foreigners, and the characteristics of the Chinese in the Four Books and Five Classics, Lao Zhuang philosophy appear in front of foreigners. And those so-called high-class Chinese who are educated in foreign countries and live in Chinese concessions, also cater to the foreigners' preferences and deliberately abstractly fabricate many mysterious things in order to deceive foreigners and arouse their curiosity, turning China into an inexplicable country. Those credulous foreigners believe that it is true, so they say that a certain Chinese celebrity said that China is like this, so it can be seen that China is like this.

Sophistry itself is not a sin, but sophistry with ulterior motives is a sin. Distorted sophistry caused unintentionally is forgivable, but sophistry caused intentionally is unforgivable. Of course, around us, there are many skins that have not yet reached the vertebrate stage, but there are also many solid and upright men standing in front of us. It is one kind of people who rushed into the school with wooden sticks and bare hands to insist on confronting the police in Beijing for several hours without retreating. It is another kind of people in Tianjin who resolutely risked their lives to fight if they were unwilling to be traitors. It is another kind of people who firmly resisted the banner in the Northeast. It is another kind of people who silently waited for the signal of national liberation in the vast wilderness of the Chinese Loess Plateau. The poet Carl Sandburg's prophecy may soon sweep over us:

The booming passion of hundreds of millions of people can rise up

to become a whirlwind; once a gust is launched, who can drive it? you? Or you? Or you? Only history, only tomorrow knows

Because every change bursts out like

A baby born of its own turbulent time

Extract a pattern that was not known before.

These many intrinsic characteristics brewed in China will naturally not be heard, seen, or tasted by our famous "China Expert," but time will always reveal the outer cover and push these brand-new facts to stimulate her eyes, the vibration of her ears, and the touch of her heart, and make her understand that "that is just China". "That is just the Chinese public."

I Stand Before a Solitary Grave 192

— Xingjian

I stand before a solitary grave,

Caressing the worn and damaged inscription, unable to read the name of the one who sleeps eternally.

Clumps of weeds cover this uneven mound of earth,

Knowing that no one has cared for this deceased traveler for a long time!

This place is a desolate wilderness beyond a lonely village,

Even if there are still signs of habitation, they are still far away;

Except for woodcutters and shepherds occasionally passing by here,

All there is is the uncaring clouds drifting leisurely,

Wild rabbits coming and going at will.

This scene fills me with melancholy and hesitation,

Arousing from the depths of my heart my aversion to death.

I do not know what kind of person this silent departed one was,

But today I offer my utmost sympathetic mourning.

You must have had a glorious history worthy of song and tears,

Yet in the annals of God's chosen people,

Not a single word or sentence can be found about you!

Born with the grasses and trees, dead and rotting with the grasses and trees,

Leaving no trace of you in this desolate world for people to remember.

Was it the difficult days of hardship and adversity that made you panic,

Eagerly longing to come here to hide?

Was it the nagging illness that robbed you of your happy days,

Therefore, you silently nodded, agreeing to tranquil death?

Was it the cruel world giving you unbearable humiliation everywhere,

Filling you with anger, and interrupting the extension of your life?

Or did the bitter cup of love cool your burning heart,

Seeking extraordinary comfort, and willingly departing alone in desolation,

Walking listlessly and coldly?

Boundaries of Life 193

— Ding

Suddenly, a letter from Xia, from a foreign country, arrived from Huang.

Four years, what a long four years!

I don't know anything about Xia's news, and Xia doesn't know my whereabouts either?

Yes, we have been out of touch for four years.

In short, since the outbreak of the "September 18th" and "January 28th" wars, the relationship of love between us has been broken, destroyed by artillery fire. The ruthless artillery fire has shattered, crushed, and eliminated all our fantasies at that time.

From that period on, our thoughts and feelings also underwent great changes along with the environment at that time.

At that time, we each had our own opinions. And our understanding of life was different, and our views were different, so we finally couldn't integrate.

Xia was very selfish for the sake of love, and she thought about everything from her own point of view. As for me, it is better to say that I was for the sake of ideals than for the sake of love, so it was often difficult to approach Xia's individualistic views.

However, Xia's personality was very stubborn. She wanted to drag me from my complicated life into her simple and gentle rosy life.

How is this possible! For the sake of love, can I sell my personality, soul and glorious ideals? If this is really necessary, then I have to sacrifice "love".

"Love," I think: should be the driving force of life. "Love" is a kind of cohesive force of mankind. This kind of cohesion, it is not for its own happiness. "Love," the force of evidence, is a force that destroys evil and darkness, and creates a great and bright life!

Therefore, I felt that Xia's love for me was dim, gray, weak, and meaningless. So the love between us finally broke and disappeared.

That's how our lives were separated in the fierce bloody battle. Xia, so went away sadly. Xia, then sadly and angrily returned to her distant foreign home that was trampled under the enemy. From then on, goodbye forever, Xia who once loved me passionately!

At that time, in the moment of parting, although my heart felt extremely painful. I believe that from now on, Xia and I will never meet again.

This matter, it is better to say that we are disappointed than disappointed in love. It is better to say that it is a failure than a success. Because - we are all separated, broken up, and fighting for our own future.

In short, from the year of the war, Xia's impression was no longer engraved in my mind, and my shadow naturally would not exist in Xia's heart. The realistic and cruel war has differentiated our lives. From then on, four years, I no longer know Xia's news. Anyway, Xia doesn't need to know me either.

Yes, four years, what a long time. I live alone. But collective struggle and work make me strong and happy. I don't feel the sadness of loneliness, and I won't be distressed because of this seeking love.

Isn't the great and infinite love of the world more glorious and happier than that person's insignificant "love"?

Four years, what a long time. But I am still living the same way. Constantly moving towards the dangerous path of life. Although during this time, I have suffered many setbacks and hit many nails. However, my heart has not died, and my heart is still burning with the flames of struggle.

But, Xia, how is she now? Now, although I received this sudden coming letter from Xia. However, Xia didn't tell me anything. However, in this simple letter from Xia, I have already tasted the sadness of the body. Although she did not express it clearly, I have already seen the traces of tears in the words between the lines of this pair of letters. Could it be that she is already disgusted with her current luxurious, decadent, degenerate and boring life as a wife? Have you already awakened?

Four years, what a long time. The paths we take are completely opposite, and they are getting farther and farther apart. We have become strangers on the journey, and even we have become irreconcilable enemies.

Now, what I want to answer to Xia, to let her understand, is that me——

"This person, Zeng Ye, loves your Lin, he has never changed his position and has never shaken his faith. He is still the same as in the past - standing on the battle line of fighting for national liberation and freedom, and fighting until the last breath!"

Parting Feelings (Continued) 194

— Yingzi

Ah! How fast ten years have passed! In this city, I quickly grew from a child into an "adult." The memories of childhood are mostly accurate. I remember how this city grew from decay and ruins. I almost saw with one glance how it slowly prospered from a state of decline and desolation. New-style buildings gradually increased, the roads were widened, and even the empty new and old city avenues were lined with many new-style factories and houses. The electric lights shone brightly, and in this prairie, the big city at dusk, the neon lights and the rattling broadcast radios flickered in the streets of the frontier at night. People's lives are also slowly changing, but the recession still deeply shrouds the city. The market for human flesh is "expanding" day by day. The lives of those small citizens who grew up with this city cannot be discussed except for corruption.

After seeing this, I, a young man, saw another scene. This time, the entire frontier prairie and city were about to be transformed into a "Paradise of the Kingly Way," right?

The planes with red ball tails also gave the people on the prairie more knowledge, and they got used to seeing them. As usual, there are always one or two circling in the blue sky every day. Breaking through the clear air, the buzzing sound it makes disturbs everyone's sense of hearing. From this sense of hearing and sight, people also heard their own "fate," but they didn't know when people would lay eggs, and they were always grumbling in their hearts: "Will they lay eggs?"

What followed was a white flag with a fluttering red ball, as if it wanted to pierce the heart of every young person. Below it was a vast courtyard called a public hall. Who knows what tricks are being played inside! "Matsuda Public Hall" and "×× Public Hall" also appear everywhere in the streets and alleys. When did this place become "someone else's" residential area?

The frontier prairie and this big city in the desert are gradually changing. It will change so much that I will not recognize its original appearance, right? And now, I am about to leave it, this city where I was born, raised, and lived for more than ten years!

Recalling the things I used to hear and see without feeling anything: the white snow on the top of Daqingshan in winter, the strings of winter bells ringing past, the flocks of sheep grazing on the green grassland, and the crows wailing in the sky at dusk... At this time, everything is unusually kind to me, and I feel attached to it.

My friends in the frontier, I wish you in advance when we meet again: "Have you been well since we last met!"

Will this not become an illusory dream?

This time, I really and truly felt the pain of "parting feelings" (End)
